  1180	    /// <summary>
  1181	    /// Regression test for https://github.com/quartznet/quartznet/issues/859
  1182	    /// GetFireTimeAfter should not mutate the trigger's StartTimeUtc field.
  1183	    /// </summary>
  1184	    [Test]
  1185	    public void GetFireTimeAfterShouldNotMutateStartTimeUtc()
  1186	    {
  1187	        DateTimeOffset originalStartTime = DateBuilder.DateOf(0, 0, 0, 1, 1, 2024);
  1188	        var trigger = new DailyTimeIntervalTriggerImpl
  1189	        {
  1190	            StartTimeUtc = originalStartTime,
  1191	            StartTimeOfDay = new TimeOfDay(8, 0, 0),
  1192	            EndTimeOfDay = new TimeOfDay(17, 0, 0),
  1193	            RepeatIntervalUnit = IntervalUnit.Hour,
  1194	            RepeatInterval = 1
  1195	        };
  1196	
  1197	        // Call with a time after the daily start time to exercise the code path
  1198	        // that previously mutated startTimeUtc
  1199	        DateTimeOffset afterTime = DateBuilder.DateOf(10, 0, 0, 1, 1, 2024);
  1200	        trigger.GetFireTimeAfter(afterTime);
  1201	
  1202	        Assert.That(trigger.StartTimeUtc, Is.EqualTo(originalStartTime),
  1203	            "StartTimeUtc should not be modified by GetFireTimeAfter");
  1204	
  1205	        // Also verify ComputeFirstFireTimeUtc doesn't mutate it
  1206	        trigger.StartTimeUtc = originalStartTime;
  1207	        trigger.ComputeFirstFireTimeUtc(null);
  1208	
  1209	        Assert.That(trigger.StartTimeUtc, Is.EqualTo(originalStartTime),
  1210	            "StartTimeUtc should not be modified by ComputeFirstFireTimeUtc");
  1211	    }

  1213	    [Test]
  1214	    public void DoNothing_WithMisfireThreshold_PreservesWithinThresholdFireTime()
  1215	    {
  1216	        var startTime = new DateTimeOffset(2025, 1, 1, 10, 0, 0, TimeSpan.Zero);
  1217	        var frozenNow = new DateTimeOffset(2025, 1, 1, 10, 2, 30, TimeSpan.Zero);
  1218	        var threshold = TimeSpan.FromSeconds(60);
  1219	
  1220	        var trigger = new DailyTimeIntervalTriggerImpl(new FixedTimeProvider(frozenNow))
  1221	        {
  1222	            Key = new TriggerKey("test", "test"),
  1223	            StartTimeUtc = startTime,
  1224	            StartTimeOfDay = new TimeOfDay(0, 0, 0),
  1225	            EndTimeOfDay = new TimeOfDay(23, 59, 59),
  1226	            RepeatInterval = 2,
  1227	            RepeatIntervalUnit = IntervalUnit.Minute,
  1228	            MisfireInstruction = MisfireInstruction.DailyTimeIntervalTrigger.DoNothing
  1229	        };
  1230	        trigger.ComputeFirstFireTimeUtc(null);
  1231	
  1232	        trigger.UpdateAfterMisfire(null, threshold);
  1233	
  1234	        DateTimeOffset? nextFire = trigger.GetNextFireTimeUtc();
  1235	        Assert.IsNotNull(nextFire);
  1236	        Assert.That(nextFire.Value, Is.EqualTo(new DateTimeOffset(2025, 1, 1, 10, 2, 0, TimeSpan.Zero)),
  1237	            "Should preserve the 10:02 fire time that is within the misfire threshold");
  1238	    }
  1239	
  1240	    private sealed class FixedTimeProvider(DateTimeOffset utcNow) : TimeProvider
  1241	    {
  1242	        public override DateTimeOffset GetUtcNow() => utcNow;
  1243	    }
  1244	}

    22	namespace Quartz;
    23	
    24	/// <summary>
    25	/// Represents a time in hour, minute and second of any given day.
    26	/// <remarks>
    27	/// <para>
    28	/// The hour is in 24-hour convention, meaning values are from 0 to 23.
    29	/// </para>
    30	/// </remarks>
    31	/// </summary>
    32	/// <seealso cref="IDailyTimeIntervalTrigger"/>
    33	/// <author>James House</author>
    34	/// <author>Zemian Deng saltnlight5@gmail.com</author>
    35	/// <author>Nuno Maia (.NET)</author>
    36	[Serializable]
    37	public sealed class TimeOfDay
    38	{
    39	    /// <summary>
    40	    /// Create a TimeOfDay instance for the given hour, minute and second.
    41	    /// </summary>
    42	    /// <param name="hour">The hour of day, between 0 and 23.</param>
    43	    /// <param name="minute">The minute of the hour, between 0 and 59.</param>
    44	    /// <param name="second">The second of the minute, between 0 and 59.</param>
    45	    public TimeOfDay(int hour, int minute, int second)
    46	    {
    47	        Hour = hour;
    48	        Minute = minute;
    49	        Second = second;
    50	        Validate();
    51	    }
    52	
    53	    /// <summary>
    54	    /// Create a TimeOfDay instance for the given hour, minute (at the zero second of the minute).
    55	    /// </summary>
    56	    /// <param name="hour">The hour of day, between 0 and 23.</param>
    57	    /// <param name="minute">The minute of the hour, between 0 and 59.</param>
    58	    public TimeOfDay(int hour, int minute)
    59	    {
    60	        Hour = hour;
    61	        Minute = minute;
    62	        Second = 0;
    63	        Validate();
    64	    }
    65	
    66	    private void Validate()
    67	    {
    68	        if (Hour < 0 || Hour > 23)
    69	        {
    70	            Throw.ArgumentException("Hour must be from 0 to 23");
    71	        }
    72	
    73	        if (Minute < 0 || Minute > 59)
    74	        {
    75	            Throw.ArgumentException("Minute must be from 0 to 59");
    76	        }
    77	
    78	        if (Second < 0 || Second > 59)
    79	        {
    80	            Throw.ArgumentException("Second must be from 0 to 59");
    81	        }
    82	    }
    83	
    84	    /// <summary>
    85	    /// Create a TimeOfDay instance for the given hour, minute and second.
    86	    /// </summary>
    87	    /// <param name="hour">The hour of day, between 0 and 23.</param>
    88	    /// <param name="minute">The minute of the hour, between 0 and 59.</param>
    89	    /// <param name="second">The second of the minute, between 0 and 59.</param>
    90	    /// <returns></returns>
    91	    public static TimeOfDay HourMinuteAndSecondOfDay(int hour, int minute, int second)
    92	    {
    93	        return new TimeOfDay(hour, minute, second);
    94	    }
    95	
    96	    /// <summary>
    97	    /// Create a TimeOfDay instance for the given hour, minute (at the zero second of the minute)..
    98	    /// </summary>
    99	    /// <param name="hour">The hour of day, between 0 and 23.</param>
   100	    /// <param name="minute">The minute of the hour, between 0 and 59.</param>
   101	    /// <returns>The newly instantiated TimeOfDay</returns>
   102	    public static TimeOfDay HourAndMinuteOfDay(int hour, int minute)
   103	    {
   104	        return new TimeOfDay(hour, minute);
   105	    }
   106	
   107	    /// <summary>
   108	    /// The hour of the day (between 0 and 23).
   109	    /// </summary>
   110	    public int Hour { get; }
   111	
   112	    /// <summary>
   113	    /// The minute of the hour (between 0 and 59).
   114	    /// </summary>
   115	    public int Minute { get; }
   116	
   117	    /// <summary>
   118	    /// The second of the minute (between 0 and 59).
   119	    /// </summary>
   120	    public int Second { get; }
   121	
   122	    /// <summary>
   123	    /// Determine with this time of day is before the given time of day.
   124	    /// </summary>
   125	    /// <param name="timeOfDay"></param>
   126	    /// <returns>True this time of day is before the given time of day.</returns>
   127	    public bool Before(TimeOfDay timeOfDay)
   128	    {
   129	        if (timeOfDay.Hour > Hour)
   130	        {
   131	            return true;
   132	        }
   133	        if (timeOfDay.Hour < Hour)
   134	        {
   135	            return false;
   136	        }
   137	
   138	        if (timeOfDay.Minute > Minute)
   139	        {
   140	            return true;
   141	        }
   142	        if (timeOfDay.Minute < Minute)
   143	        {
   144	            return false;
   145	        }
   146	
   147	        if (timeOfDay.Second > Second)
   148	        {
   149	            return true;
   150	        }
   151	        if (timeOfDay.Second < Second)
   152	        {
   153	            return false;
   154	        }
   155	
   156	        return false; // must be equal...
   157	    }
   158	
   159	    public override bool Equals(object? obj)
   160	    {
   161	        if (obj is not TimeOfDay timeOfDay)
   162	        {
   163	            return false;
   164	        }
   165	
   166	        return timeOfDay.Hour == Hour && timeOfDay.Minute == Minute && timeOfDay.Second == Second;
   167	    }
   168	
   169	    public override int GetHashCode()
   170	    {
   171	        return (Hour + 1) ^ (Minute + 1) ^ (Second + 1);
   172	    }
   173	
   174	    /// <summary>
   175	    /// Return a date with time of day reset to this object values. The millisecond value will be zero.
   176	    /// </summary>
   177	    /// <param name="dateTime"></param>
   178	    public DateTimeOffset? GetTimeOfDayForDate(DateTimeOffset? dateTime)
   179	    {
   180	        if (dateTime is null)
   181	        {
   182	            return null;
   183	        }
   184	
   185	        return GetTimeOfDayForDate(dateTime.Value);
   186	    }
   187	
   188	    /// <summary>
   189	    /// Return a date with time of day reset to this object values. The millisecond value will be zero.
   190	    /// </summary>
   191	    /// <param name="dateTime"></param>
   192	    public DateTimeOffset GetTimeOfDayForDate(DateTimeOffset dateTime)
   193	    {
   194	        DateTimeOffset cal = new DateTimeOffset(dateTime.Date, dateTime.Offset);
   195	        TimeSpan t = new TimeSpan(0, Hour, Minute, Second);
   196	        return cal.Add(t);
   197	    }
   198	
   199	    public override string ToString()
   200	    {
   201	        return "TimeOfDay[" + Hour + ":" + Minute + ":" + Second + "]";
   202	    }
   203	}

    52	#pragma warning disable CA2211
    53	    public static Func<string, TimeZoneInfo?> CustomResolver = id => null;
    54	#pragma warning restore CA2211
    55	
    56	    /// <summary>
    57	    /// TimeZoneInfo.ConvertTime is not supported under mono
    58	    /// </summary>
    59	    /// <param name="dateTimeOffset"></param>
    60	    /// <param name="timeZoneInfo"></param>
    61	    /// <returns></returns>
    62	    public static DateTimeOffset ConvertTime(DateTimeOffset dateTimeOffset, TimeZoneInfo timeZoneInfo)
    63	    {
    64	        return TimeZoneInfo.ConvertTime(dateTimeOffset, timeZoneInfo);
    65	    }
    66	
    67	    /// <summary>
    68	    /// TimeZoneInfo.GetUtcOffset(DateTimeOffset) is not supported under mono
    69	    /// </summary>
    70	    /// <param name="dateTimeOffset"></param>
    71	    /// <param name="timeZoneInfo"></param>
    72	    /// <returns></returns>
    73	    public static TimeSpan GetUtcOffset(DateTimeOffset dateTimeOffset, TimeZoneInfo timeZoneInfo)
    74	    {
    75	        if (QuartzEnvironment.IsRunningOnMono)
    76	        {
    77	            return timeZoneInfo.GetUtcOffset(dateTimeOffset.UtcDateTime);
    78	        }
    79	
    80	        return timeZoneInfo.GetUtcOffset(dateTimeOffset);
    81	    }
    82	
    83	    public static TimeSpan GetUtcOffset(DateTime dateTime, TimeZoneInfo timeZoneInfo)
    84	    {
    85	        // Unlike the default behavior of TimeZoneInfo.GetUtcOffset, it is prefered to choose
    86	        // the DAYLIGHT time when the input is ambiguous, because the daylight instance is the
    87	        // FIRST instance, and time moves in a forward direction.
    88	
    89	        TimeSpan offset = timeZoneInfo.IsAmbiguousTime(dateTime)
    90	            ? timeZoneInfo.GetAmbiguousTimeOffsets(dateTime).Max()
    91	            : timeZoneInfo.GetUtcOffset(dateTime);
    92	
    93	        return offset;
    94	    }
    95	
    96	    /// <summary>
    97	    /// Tries to find time zone with given id, has ability do some fallbacks when necessary.
    98	    /// </summary>
    99	    /// <param name="id">System id of the time zone.</param>
   100	    /// <returns></returns>
   101	    public static TimeZoneInfo FindTimeZoneById(string id)
   102	    {
   103	        TimeZoneInfo? info = null;
   104	        try
   105	        {
   106	            info = TimeZoneInfo.FindSystemTimeZoneById(id);
   107	        }
   108	        catch (TimeZoneNotFoundException ex)
   109	        {
   110	            if (timeZoneIdAliases.TryGetValue(id, out var aliasedId))
   111	            {
   112	                try
   113	                {
   114	                    info = TimeZoneInfo.FindSystemTimeZoneById(aliasedId);
   115	                }
   116	                catch
   117	                {
   118	                    var logger = LogProvider.CreateLogger(nameof(TimeZoneUtil));
   119	                    logger.LogError("Could not find time zone using alias id {AliasId}", aliasedId);
   120	                }
   121	            }
   122	
   123	            if (info is null)
   124	            {
   125	                info = CustomResolver(id);
   126	            }
   127	
   128	            if (info is null)
   129	            {
   130	                // we tried our best
   131	                throw new TimeZoneNotFoundException(
   132	                    $"Could not find time zone with id {id}, consider using Quartz.Plugins.TimeZoneConverter for resolving more time zones ids",
   133	                    ex);
   134	            }
   135	        }
   136	
   137	        return info;
   138	    }
   139	}

2026-05-29 09:34:14,918 - INFO - swea-agent - 💭 THOUGHT
Good, the existing tests pass. Now let me write a quick reproduction based on the PR description. Let me create a small test program

🎬 ACTION
cd /testbed && cat > /tmp/test_dst.cs << 'EOF'
using System;
using System.Linq;
using Quartz;
using Quartz.Impl.Triggers;
using Quartz.Spi;

public class TestDst
{
    public static void Main()
    {
        // Reproduce the issue from the PR description
        DateTime startDateTime = new DateTime(2020, 10, 25);
        DateTimeOffset startDateTimeOffset = new DateTimeOffset(startDateTime);
        int daysAhead = 3;

        TriggerBuilder triggerBuilder = TriggerBuilder.Create()
            .WithIdentity("id")
            .ForJob("job")
            .StartAt(new DateTimeOffset(startDateTime.AddMinutes(1).AddSeconds(5)))
            .WithDailyTimeIntervalSchedule(
                scheduleBuilder =>
                {
                    scheduleBuilder.OnEveryDay().WithIntervalInHours(24);
                    scheduleBuilder
                        .StartingDailyAt(new TimeOfDay(0, 1, 5))
                        .EndingDailyAt(new TimeOfDay(23, 59, 59))
                        .WithMisfireHandlingInstructionDoNothing();
                });

        IReadOnlyList<DateTimeOffset> fireTimes =
            TriggerUtils.ComputeFireTimesBetween(
            (IOperableTrigger)triggerBuilder.Build(),
            null,
            startDateTimeOffset,
            startDateTimeOffset.AddDays(daysAhead));

        Console.WriteLine($"Number of fire times: {fireTimes.Count}");
        foreach (var ft in fireTimes)
        {
            Console.WriteLine($"  {ft} (Local: {ft.LocalDateTime})");
        }
        
        Console.WriteLine();
        
        var expected0 = new DateTimeOffset(new DateTime(2020, 10, 25, 0, 1, 5));
        var expected1 = new DateTimeOffset(new DateTime(2020, 10, 26, 0, 1, 5));
        var expected2 = new DateTimeOffset(new DateTime(2020, 10, 27, 0, 1, 5));
        
        Console.WriteLine($"Expected 3, got {fireTimes.Count}");
        bool firstOk = fireTimes.First().LocalDateTime == expected0.LocalDateTime;
        bool secondOk = fireTimes.Skip(1).First().LocalDateTime == expected1.LocalDateTime;
        bool thirdOk = fireTimes.Skip(2).First().LocalDateTime == expected2.LocalDateTime;
        
        Console.WriteLine($"First: {firstOk} (expected {expected0.LocalDateTime}, got {fireTimes.First().LocalDateTime})");
        if (fireTimes.Count > 1)
            Console.WriteLine($"Second: {secondOk} (expected {expected1.LocalDateTime}, got {fireTimes.Skip(1).First().LocalDateTime})");
        if (fireTimes.Count > 2)
            Console.WriteLine($"Third: {thirdOk} (expected {expected2.LocalDateTime}, got {fireTimes.Skip(2).First().LocalDateTime})");
        if (fireTimes.Count > 3)
            Console.WriteLine($"Extra: {fireTimes.Skip(3).First().LocalDateTime}");
    }
}
EOF

cd /testbed && cat > /tmp/test_repro.cs << 'ENDOFPROGRAM'
using System;
using System.Linq;
using Quartz;
using Quartz.Impl.Triggers;
using Quartz.Spi;

public class TestRepro
{
    public static void Main()
    {
        // Reproduce the issue from the PR description
        DateTime startDateTime = new DateTime(2020, 10, 25);
        DateTimeOffset startDateTimeOffset = new DateTimeOffset(startDateTime);
        int daysAhead = 3;

        TriggerBuilder triggerBuilder = TriggerBuilder.Create()
            .WithIdentity("id")
            .ForJob("job")
            .StartAt(new DateTimeOffset(startDateTime.AddMinutes(1).AddSeconds(5)))
            .WithDailyTimeIntervalSchedule(
                scheduleBuilder =>
                {
                    scheduleBuilder.OnEveryDay().WithIntervalInHours(24);
                    scheduleBuilder
                        .StartingDailyAt(new TimeOfDay(0, 1, 5))
                        .EndingDailyAt(new TimeOfDay(23, 59, 59))
                        .WithMisfireHandlingInstructionDoNothing();
                });

        IReadOnlyList<DateTimeOffset> fireTimes =
            TriggerUtils.ComputeFireTimesBetween(
            (IOperableTrigger)triggerBuilder.Build(),
            null,
            startDateTimeOffset,
            startDateTimeOffset.AddDays(daysAhead));

        Console.WriteLine($"Number of fire times: {fireTimes.Count}");
        foreach (var ft in fireTimes)
        {
            Console.WriteLine($"  {ft} (Local: {ft.LocalDateTime}, UTC: {ft.UtcDateTime})");
        }
        
        Console.WriteLine();
        
        if (fireTimes.Count == 3)
        {
            Console.WriteLine("PASS: Got exactly 3 fire times");
        }
        else
        {
            Console.WriteLine($"FAIL: Expected 3 fire times, got {fireTimes.Count}");
        }

        var expected0 = new DateTimeOffset(new DateTime(2020, 10, 25, 0, 1, 5));
        var expected1 = new DateTimeOffset(new DateTime(2020, 10, 26, 0, 1, 5));
        var expected2 = new DateTimeOffset(new DateTime(2020, 10, 27, 0, 1, 5));
        
        Console.WriteLine($"First:  expected={expected0.LocalDateTime}, got={fireTimes[0].LocalDateTime}, match={fireTimes[0].LocalDateTime == expected0.LocalDateTime}");
        Console.WriteLine($"Second: expected={expected1.LocalDateTime}, got={fireTimes[1].LocalDateTime}, match={fireTimes[1].LocalDateTime == expected1.LocalDateTime}");
        Console.WriteLine($"Third:  expected={expected2.LocalDateTime}, got={fireTimes[2].LocalDateTime}, match={fireTimes[2].LocalDateTime == expected2.LocalDateTime}");
        if (fireTimes.Count > 3)
        {
            Console.WriteLine($"Extra:  {fireTimes[3].LocalDateTime}");
        }
    }
}
ENDOFPROGRAM

using System;
using System.Collections.Generic;
using System.Linq;
using Quartz;
using Quartz.Spi;

DateTime startDateTime = new DateTime(2020, 10, 25);
DateTimeOffset startDateTimeOffset = new DateTimeOffset(startDateTime);
int daysAhead = 3;

TriggerBuilder triggerBuilder = TriggerBuilder.Create()
    .WithIdentity("id")
    .ForJob("job")
    .StartAt(new DateTimeOffset(startDateTime.AddMinutes(1).AddSeconds(5)))
    .WithDailyTimeIntervalSchedule(
        scheduleBuilder =>
        {
            scheduleBuilder.OnEveryDay().WithIntervalInHours(24);
            scheduleBuilder
                .StartingDailyAt(new TimeOfDay(0, 1, 5))
                .EndingDailyAt(new TimeOfDay(23, 59, 59))
                .WithMisfireHandlingInstructionDoNothing();
        });

IReadOnlyList<DateTimeOffset> fireTimes =
    TriggerUtils.ComputeFireTimesBetween(
    (IOperableTrigger)triggerBuilder.Build(),
    null,
    startDateTimeOffset,
    startDateTimeOffset.AddDays(daysAhead));

Console.WriteLine($"Number of fire times: {fireTimes.Count}");
foreach (var ft in fireTimes)
{
    Console.WriteLine($"  {ft} (Local: {ft.LocalDateTime}, UTC: {ft.UtcDateTime})");
}

Console.WriteLine();

if (fireTimes.Count == 3)
{
    Console.WriteLine("PASS: Got exactly 3 fire times");
}
else
{
    Console.WriteLine($"FAIL: Expected 3 fire times, got {fireTimes.Count}");
}

var expected0 = new DateTimeOffset(new DateTime(2020, 10, 25, 0, 1, 5));
var expected1 = new DateTimeOffset(new DateTime(2020, 10, 26, 0, 1, 5));
var expected2 = new DateTimeOffset(new DateTime(2020, 10, 27, 0, 1, 5));

Console.WriteLine($"Second: expected={expected1}, got={fireTimes[1]}, match={fireTimes[1] == expected1}");
Console.WriteLine($"Third:  expected={expected2}, got={fireTimes[2]}, match={fireTimes[2] == expected2}");
if (fireTimes.Count > 3)
{
    Console.WriteLine($"Extra:  {fireTimes[3]}");
}

🎬 ACTION
cat > /tmp/test_repro/Program.cs << 'ENDOFPROGRAM'
using System;
using System.Collections.Generic;
using System.Linq;
using Quartz;
using Quartz.Spi;
using Quartz.Util;

// Use "GMT Standard Time" which has DST change on Oct 25, 2020
// "GMT Standard Time" is the Windows ID for UK time (Europe/London)
var tz = TimeZoneUtil.FindTimeZoneById("GMT Standard Time");

DateTime startDateTime = new DateTime(2020, 10, 25);
DateTimeOffset startDateTimeOffset = new DateTimeOffset(startDateTime);
int daysAhead = 3;

TriggerBuilder triggerBuilder = TriggerBuilder.Create()
    .WithIdentity("id")
    .ForJob("job")
    .StartAt(new DateTimeOffset(startDateTime.AddMinutes(1).AddSeconds(5)))
    .WithDailyTimeIntervalSchedule(
        scheduleBuilder =>
        {
            scheduleBuilder.OnEveryDay().WithIntervalInHours(24);
            scheduleBuilder
                .StartingDailyAt(new TimeOfDay(0, 1, 5))
                .EndingDailyAt(new TimeOfDay(23, 59, 59))
                .WithMisfireHandlingInstructionDoNothing();
        });

var trigger = (IOperableTrigger)triggerBuilder.Build();
// Set the timezone
if (trigger is DailyTimeIntervalTriggerImpl dailyTrigger)
{
    dailyTrigger.TimeZone = tz;
}

IReadOnlyList<DateTimeOffset> fireTimes =
    TriggerUtils.ComputeFireTimesBetween(
    trigger,
    null,
    startDateTimeOffset,
    startDateTimeOffset.AddDays(daysAhead));

Console.WriteLine($"Number of fire times: {fireTimes.Count}");
foreach (var ft in fireTimes)
{
    Console.WriteLine($"  {ft} (Local: {ft.LocalDateTime}, UTC: {ft.UtcDateTime})");
}

Console.WriteLine();

if (fireTimes.Count == 3)
{
    Console.WriteLine("PASS: Got exactly 3 fire times");
}
else
{
    Console.WriteLine($"FAIL: Expected 3 fire times, got {fireTimes.Count}");
    // Show the extra ones
    for (int i = 0; i < fireTimes.Count; i++)
    {
        Console.WriteLine($"  [{i}]: {fireTimes[i]} -> local: {fireTimes[i].LocalDateTime}, utc: {fireTimes[i].UtcDateTime}");
    }
}
ENDOFPROGRAM

In that timezone, the clocks go back from summer time (GMT+2/BST+1) to winter time (GMT+1/GMT). The extra fire time at 23:01:05 on October 25 suggests the issue is related to the "fall back" transition where there's a duplicated hour.

Let me try with a timezone that actually has a DST transition on Oct 25, 2020. "Central European Standard Time" (CET) is GMT+1 in winter and GMT+2 in summer. DST ends on Oct 25, 2020.

cat > /tmp/test_repro/Program.cs << 'ENDOFPROGRAM'
using System;
using System.Collections.Generic;
using System.Linq;
using Quartz;
using Quartz.Impl.Triggers;
using Quartz.Spi;
using Quartz.Util;

// Try with "Central European Standard Time" 
// In 2020, DST ends on Oct 25 at 3:00 AM CEST -> 2:00 AM CET
var tz = TimeZoneUtil.FindTimeZoneById("Central European Standard Time");

Console.WriteLine($"Timezone: {tz.Id}, {tz.DisplayName}");
Console.WriteLine($"DST change rules: {tz.GetAdjustmentRules().Length} rules");
foreach (var rule in tz.GetAdjustmentRules())
{
    Console.WriteLine($"  Rule: Start={rule.DateStart}, End={rule.DateEnd}, Delta={rule.DaylightDelta}, TransitionStart: {rule.DaylightTransitionStart}, TransitionEnd: {rule.DaylightTransitionEnd}");
}

DateTime startDateTime = new DateTime(2020, 10, 25);
DateTimeOffset startDateTimeOffset = new DateTimeOffset(startDateTime);
int daysAhead = 3;

TriggerBuilder triggerBuilder = TriggerBuilder.Create()
    .WithIdentity("id")
    .ForJob("job")
    .StartAt(new DateTimeOffset(startDateTime.AddMinutes(1).AddSeconds(5)))
    .WithDailyTimeIntervalSchedule(
        scheduleBuilder =>
        {
            scheduleBuilder.OnEveryDay().WithIntervalInHours(24);
            scheduleBuilder
                .StartingDailyAt(new TimeOfDay(0, 1, 5))
                .EndingDailyAt(new TimeOfDay(23, 59, 59))
                .WithMisfireHandlingInstructionDoNothing();
        });

var trigger = (IOperableTrigger)triggerBuilder.Build();
// Set the timezone
if (trigger is DailyTimeIntervalTriggerImpl dailyTrigger)
{
    dailyTrigger.TimeZone = tz;
}

Console.WriteLine($"Trigger StartTimeUtc: {trigger.StartTimeUtc}");
Console.WriteLine($"Trigger EndTimeUtc: {trigger.EndTimeUtc}");
Console.WriteLine($"Trigger TimeZone: {(trigger as DailyTimeIntervalTriggerImpl)?.TimeZone.Id}");

IReadOnlyList<DateTimeOffset> fireTimes =
    TriggerUtils.ComputeFireTimesBetween(
    trigger,
    null,
    startDateTimeOffset,
    startDateTimeOffset.AddDays(daysAhead));

Console.WriteLine($"\nNumber of fire times: {fireTimes.Count}");
for (int i = 0; i < fireTimes.Count; i++)
{
    var ft = fireTimes[i];
    // Convert to the target timezone for display
    var local = TimeZoneInfo.ConvertTime(ft, tz);
    Console.WriteLine($"  [{i}]: {ft} -> UTC: {ft.UtcDateTime}, TZ local: {local}");
}

Console.WriteLine();

if (fireTimes.Count == 3)
{
    Console.WriteLine("PASS: Got exactly 3 fire times");
}
else
{
    Console.WriteLine($"FAIL: Expected 3 fire times, got {fireTimes.Count}");
}
ENDOFPROGRAM

using System;
using System.Collections.Generic;
using System.Linq;
using Quartz;
using Quartz.Impl.Triggers;
using Quartz.Spi;
using Quartz.Util;

// Try with "Central European Standard Time" 
var tz = TimeZoneUtil.FindTimeZoneById("Central European Standard Time");

DateTime startDateTime = new DateTime(2020, 10, 25);
DateTimeOffset startDateTimeOffset = new DateTimeOffset(startDateTime);
int daysAhead = 3;

TriggerBuilder triggerBuilder = TriggerBuilder.Create()
    .WithIdentity("id")
    .ForJob("job")
    .StartAt(new DateTimeOffset(startDateTime.AddMinutes(1).AddSeconds(5)))
    .WithDailyTimeIntervalSchedule(
        scheduleBuilder =>
        {
            scheduleBuilder.OnEveryDay().WithIntervalInHours(24);
            scheduleBuilder
                .StartingDailyAt(new TimeOfDay(0, 1, 5))
                .EndingDailyAt(new TimeOfDay(23, 59, 59))
                .WithMisfireHandlingInstructionDoNothing();
        });

var trigger = (IOperableTrigger)triggerBuilder.Build();
if (trigger is DailyTimeIntervalTriggerImpl dailyTrigger)
{
    dailyTrigger.TimeZone = tz;
}

Console.WriteLine($"Trigger StartTimeUtc: {trigger.StartTimeUtc}");
Console.WriteLine($"Trigger TimeZone: {tz.Id}");

// Let's trace GetFireTimeAfter calls manually
var dt = (DailyTimeIntervalTriggerImpl)trigger;

// Simulate ComputeFirstFireTimeUtc:
var startMinus1 = trigger.StartTimeUtc.AddSeconds(-1);
Console.WriteLine($"\nStartTimeUtc - 1s: {startMinus1}");

var ft1 = dt.GetFireTimeAfter(startMinus1);
Console.WriteLine($"GetFireTimeAfter(start-1s) = {ft1} (UTC), {ft1?.ToUniversalTime()}");

if (ft1 != null)
{
    var ft2 = dt.GetFireTimeAfter(ft1);
    Console.WriteLine($"GetFireTimeAfter(ft1) = {ft2} (UTC), {ft2?.ToUniversalTime()}");
    
    if (ft2 != null)
    {
        var ft3 = dt.GetFireTimeAfter(ft2);
        Console.WriteLine($"GetFireTimeAfter(ft2) = {ft3} (UTC), {ft3?.ToUniversalTime()}");
        
        if (ft3 != null)
        {
            var ft4 = dt.GetFireTimeAfter(ft3);
            Console.WriteLine($"GetFireTimeAfter(ft3) = {ft4} (UTC), {ft4?.ToUniversalTime()}");
        }
    }
}

// Also check the transition
Console.WriteLine($"\nDST check:");
Console.WriteLine($"  Oct 24 22:01:05 UTC in CET: {TimeZoneInfo.ConvertTime(new DateTimeOffset(2020, 10, 24, 22, 1, 5, TimeSpan.Zero), tz)}");
Console.WriteLine($"  Oct 25 22:01:05 UTC in CET: {TimeZoneInfo.ConvertTime(new DateTimeOffset(2020, 10, 25, 22, 1, 5, TimeSpan.Zero), tz)}");

Console.WriteLine($"  Oct 26 23:01:05 UTC in CET: {TimeZoneInfo.ConvertTime(new DateTimeOffset(2020, 10, 26, 23, 1, 5, TimeSpan.Zero), tz)}");

// What's the UTC offset for Oct 25 00:01:05 local?
var oct25local = new DateTime(2020, 10, 25, 0, 1, 5);
Console.WriteLine($"\n  Oct 25 00:01:05 local (unspecified) -> UTC offset: {tz.GetUtcOffset(oct25local)}");
Console.WriteLine($"  Oct 25 00:01:05 local -> UTC: {new DateTimeOffset(oct25local, tz.GetUtcOffset(oct25local)).ToUniversalTime()}");

So the offset is +02:00 (still summer time).\n\nSo `fireTimeStartDate` becomes 2020-10-25 00:01:05 +02:00.\n\nThen `sTime = fireTimeStartDate.ToUniversalTime()` = 2020-10-24 22:01:05 UTC.\n\nThen the interval calculation:\n- `secondsAfterStart = (fireTime - startOfDayUtc).TotalSeconds` where `startOfDayUtc = TimeZoneUtil.ConvertTime(fireTimeStartDate, TimeZone)`\n\n`fireTimeStartDate` = 2020-10-25 00:01:05 +02:00.\n`TimeZoneUtil.ConvertTime(fireTimeStartDate, TimeZone)` = `TimeZoneInfo.ConvertTime(2020-10-25 00:01:05 +02:00, CET)`. This converts the DateTimeOffset to the target timezone. The input has UTC = 2020-10-24 22:01:05. The CET offset at that UTC time is +02:00. So output = 2020-10-25 00:01:05 +02:00 (same thing). So `startOfDayUtc` = 2020-10-25 00:01:05 +02:00.\n\nBut `fireTime` is 2020-10-25 23:01:06 +01:00 (CET). The UTC of this is 2020-10-25 22:01:06.\n\nNow `secondsAfterStart = (fireTime - startOfDayUtc).TotalSeconds`. But these are DateTimeOffsets with different offsets! `fireTime` = 2020-10-25 23:01:06 +01:00, `startOfDayUtc` = 2020-10-25 00:01:05 +02:00.\n\nThe subtraction of DateTimeOffsets accounts for the offset difference. So:\n- fireTime UTC = 2020-10-25 22:01:06\n- startOfDayUtc UTC = 2020-10-24 22:01:05\n- Difference = 24 hours + 1 second = 86401 seconds\n\nThen `jumpCount = secondsAfterStart / (24 * 3600)` = 86401 / 86400 = 1 (integer division). \n`secondsAfterStart % (24 * 3600)` = 86401 % 86400 = 1, which is != 0, so jumpCount++ → jumpCount = 2.\n\nSo `sTime = sTime.AddHours(24 * 2)` = 2020-10-24 22:01:05 UTC + 48h = 2020-10-26 22:01:05 UTC.\n\nThen `fireTime = TimeZoneUtil.ConvertTime(sTime, TimeZone)` = Convert 2020-10-26 22:01:05 UTC to CET. Oct 26 is in winter time (CET, +01:00). So output = 2020-10-26 23:01:05 +01:00.\n\nThen we return `fireTime?.ToUniversalTime()` = 2020-10-26 23:01:05 UTC.\n\nBut the expected result should be 2020-10-26 23:01:05 UTC (which is 2020-10-27 00:01:05 CET). Wait, actually we got 4 fire times and expected 3. Let me look at the output again:\n\n```\n[0]: 10/25/2020 22:01:05 +00:00 -> TZ local: 10/25/2020 23:01:05 +01:00\n[1]: 10/25/2020 23:01:05 +00:00 -> TZ local: 10/26/2020 00:01:05 +01:00\n[2]: 10/26/2020 23:01:05 +00:00 -> TZ local: 10/27/2020 00:01:05 +01:00\n[3]: 10/27/2020 23:01:05 +00:00 -> TZ local: 10/28/2020 00:01:05 +01:00\n```\n\nExpected (3 fire times for Oct 25, 26, 27):\n```\nOct 25 00:01:05 CEST = Oct 24 22:01:05 UTC\nOct 26 00:01:05 CET = Oct 25 23:01:05 UTC\nOct 27 00:01:05 CET = Oct 26 23:01:05 UTC\n```\n\nBut we got 4:\n```\n[0]: 10/25 22:01:05 UTC = Oct 25 23:01:05 CET (NOT expected)\n[1]: 10/25 23:01:05 UTC = Oct 26 00:01:05 CET (expected)\n[2]: 10/26 23:01:05 UTC = Oct 27 00:01:05 CET (expected)\n[3]: 10/27 23:01:05 UTC = Oct 28 00:01:05 CET (NOT expected)\n```\n\nSo the first fire time is wrong: Oct 25 23:01:05 CET instead of Oct 25 00:01:05 CEST. And there\'s an extra one on Oct 28.\n\nThe issue is in `GetFireTimeAfter`. The first call gives the wrong time because:\n- The `startTimeUtc` is 2020-10-25 00:01:05 UTC (which is Oct 25 02:01:05 CEST)\n- After converting to CET, we get fireTime = 2020-10-25 02:01:05 CEST (after the start time of day 00:01:05)\n- The jump count calculation gives jumpCount = 1, so it adds 24 hours to the startOfDay in UTC.\n- But adding 24 hours to 2020-10-24 22:01:05 UTC = 2020-10-25 22:01:05 UTC, which converts to 2020-10-25 23:01:05 CET.\n\nBut the first fire time should be at 2020-10-25 00:01:05 CEST = 2020-10-24 22:01:05 UTC. The problem is that `afterTime` (02:01:05 CEST) is after `fireTimeStartDate` (00:01:05 CEST), so it tries to find the next interval. With 24-hour interval, the next one after startOfDay would be 24 hours later, which is 2020-10-26 00:01:05 (but since DST changes, it\'s 2020-10-25 23:01:05 UTC = 2020-10-26 00:01:05 CET). But 2020-10-25 00:01:05 CEST should be THE first fire time, it\'s just that the trigger\'s startTimeUtc is set to 2020-10-25 00:01:05 UTC = 2020-10-25 02:01:05 CEST, which is AFTER the startTimeOfDay for that day.\n\nSo actually, the PR\'s scenario has `StartAt` = `startDateTime.AddMinutes(1).AddSeconds(5)` = 2020-10-25 00:01:05 UTC. And `startDateTimeOffset` = 2020-10-25 00:00:00 UTC.\n\nThe trigger\'s StartTimeUtc is 2020-10-25 00:01:05 UTC. And the query range is [2020-10-25 00:00:00 UTC, 2020-10-28 00:00:00 UTC].\n\nNow, `ComputeFireTimesBetween`:\n- Since `nextFireTimeUtc` is null, it computes first fire time.\n- But before that, it checks if `t.StartTimeUtc < from || t.StartTimeUtc > to`. StartTimeUtc = 2020-10-25 00:01:05 UTC, from = 2020-10-25 00:00:00 UTC. So `StartTimeUtc > from` is true, and StartTimeUtc is NOT changed.\n\nThen `ComputeFirstFireTimeUtc` calls `GetFireTimeAfter(StartTimeUtc.AddSeconds(-1))` = `GetFireTimeAfter(2020-10-25 00:01:04 UTC)`.\n\nIn `GetFireTimeAfter`:\n- `afterTime` = 2020-10-25 00:01:04 UTC + 1s = 2020-10-25 00:01:05 UTC\n- Check: `afterTime < startTimeUtc`? No, it\'s equal.\n- `afterTime = TimeZoneUtil.ConvertTime(2020-10-25 00:01:05 UTC, CET)` = 2020-10-25 02:01:05 CEST.\n\nNow, the startTimeOfDay is 00:01:05. The first fire time on Oct 25 should be 00:01:05 CEST = 2020-10-24 22:01:05 UTC. But since afterTime (02:01:05 CEST) is after startTimeOfDay (00:01:05 CEST), the code computes the next interval after startTimeOfDay.\n\nThe issue is that the algorithm converts afterTime to local time, then checks if it\'s before startTimeOfDay. Since it\'s after, it computes the next interval jump. With 24-hour interval, the next jump from startTimeOfDay (00:01:05) is 24 hours later = 2020-10-26 00:01:05. But due to DST, 24 hours later from Oct 25 00:01:05 CEST is Oct 26 00:01:05 CET (which is only 23 hours later in UTC).\n\nActually, the core problem might be simpler. Let me look at the `AddHours(24)` calculation more carefully.\n\n`sTime = fireTimeStartDate.ToUniversalTime()` = 2020-10-24 22:01:05 UTC (since fireTimeStartDate = 2020-10-25 00:01:05 +02:00).\n\n`sTime.AddHours(24)` = 2020-10-25 22:01:05 UTC.\n\n`TimeZoneUtil.ConvertTime(2020-10-25 22:01:05 UTC, CET)` = 2020-10-25 23:01:05 CET (offset +01:00, winter time).\n\nSo the algorithm computes the next fire time as Oct 25 23:01:05 CET (which is Oct 26 00:01:05 CET... wait, 23:01:05 + 1 hour = 00:01:05 next day? No, 23:01:05 CET is just 11:01 PM on Oct 25 in CET).\n\nActually the local time is 23:01:05, not 00:01:05. So the fire time is 23:01:05 local time, which is wrong. The expected fire time should be 00:01:05 local time.\n\nSo the bug is: when `AddHours(24)` is done on UTC time, and the DST transition happens, the resulting local time is not 24 hours later in local time but 23 hours later (because the offset changed from +02:00 to +01:00).\n\nThe algorithm should be using local time for the interval addition, not UTC time. Let me look at `GetTimeOfDayForDate`:
```csharp
public DateTimeOffset GetTimeOfDayForDate(DateTimeOffset dateTime)
{
    DateTimeOffset cal = new DateTimeOffset(dateTime.Date, dateTime.Offset);
    TimeSpan t = new TimeSpan(0, Hour, Minute, Second);
    return cal.Add(t);
}
```

It uses the offset from the passed-in dateTime. So if `fireTime.Value` is 2020-10-25 23:01:06 CET (+01:00), then `fireTimeStartDate` = 2020-10-25 00:01:05 +01:00.

Then `sTime = fireTimeStartDate.ToUniversalTime()` = 2020-10-24 23:01:05 UTC.

Now `secondsAfterStart = (fireTime - startOfDayUtc).TotalSeconds`. 
`fireTime` = 2020-10-25 23:01:06 CET (offset +01:00) = 2020-10-25 22:01:06 UTC.
`startOfDayUtc = TimeZoneUtil.ConvertTime(fireTimeStartDate, TimeZone)` = convert 2020-10-25 00:01:05 +01:00 to CET timezone = 2020-10-25 00:01:05 CET. But wait, `ConvertTime` on a DateTimeOffset just changes the offset. Actually `TimeZoneInfo.ConvertTime(DateTimeOffset, TimeZoneInfo)` returns a DateTimeOffset with the UTC time preserved but offset changed to the timezone's offset at that UTC time. 

So `startOfDayUtc = ConvertTime(2020-10-25 00:01:05 +01:00, CET)` = same UTC time but offset is CET's offset at that UTC time. The UTC time is 2020-10-24 23:01:05. The CET offset at 2020-10-24 23:01:05 UTC is... actually 2020-10-25 00:01:05 CET corresponds to 2020-10-24 22:01:05 UTC? No wait, let me recalculate.

`fireTimeStartDate` = 2020-10-25 00:01:05 +01:00. This means the DateTime is Oct 25 00:01:05 and the offset is +01:00 from UTC, so UTC = Oct 24 23:01:05.

`TimeZoneUtil.ConvertTime(2020-10-25 00:01:05 +01:00, CET)` → This converts to the CET timezone. The UTC time of the input is Oct 24 23:01:05. At that UTC time, what is the CET offset? Oct 24 23:01:05 UTC = Oct 25 01:01:05 CEST (since CEST is +02:00, and DST ends at 3:00 AM CEST on Oct 25). So the output is Oct 25 01:01:05 +02:00.

Wait, but the original intent was that `startOfDayUtc` should represent the start of day (00:01:05) in the target timezone. There's a problem here!

Let me look at this part of the code more carefully:

```csharp

// apply the proper offset for the start date
```

`fireTime.Value` is in the target timezone (CET). `GetTimeOfDayForDate` creates a DateTimeOffset with the same date and offset as fireTime. So `fireTimeStartDate` = 2020-10-25 00:01:05 with offset +01:00 (the offset from fireTime which is in CET).

Then `TimeZoneUtil.GetUtcOffset(fireTimeStartDate.DateTime, TimeZone)` is called. `fireTimeStartDate.DateTime` is 2020-10-25 00:01:05 (DateTime without offset). The CET offset at that local time... Oct 25 00:01:05 in CET zone: is it CEST (+02:00) or CET (+01:00)? 

Looking at `TimeZoneUtil.GetUtcOffset(DateTime, TimeZoneInfo)`:
```csharp
public static TimeSpan GetUtcOffset(DateTime dateTime, TimeZoneInfo timeZoneInfo)
{
    TimeSpan offset = timeZoneInfo.IsAmbiguousTime(dateTime)
        ? timeZoneInfo.GetAmbiguousTimeOffsets(dateTime).Max()
        : timeZoneInfo.GetUtcOffset(dateTime);
    return offset;
}
```

On Oct 25 2020 at 00:01:05, the time is NOT ambiguous (ambiguity only happens in the overlap period after DST ends, i.e., between 2:00 AM and 3:00 AM). So the offset is +02:00 (still summer time).

So `fireTimeStartDate` becomes 2020-10-25 00:01:05 +02:00.

Then `sTime = fireTimeStartDate.ToUniversalTime()` = 2020-10-24 22:01:05 UTC.

Then the interval calculation:
- `secondsAfterStart = (fireTime - startOfDayUtc).TotalSeconds` where `startOfDayUtc = TimeZoneUtil.ConvertTime(fireTimeStartDate, TimeZone)`

`fireTimeStartDate` = 2020-10-25 00:01:05 +02:00.
`TimeZoneUtil.ConvertTime(fireTimeStartDate, TimeZone)` = `TimeZoneInfo.ConvertTime(2020-10-25 00:01:05 +02:00, CET)`. This converts the DateTimeOffset to the target timezone. The input has UTC = 2020-10-24 22:01:05. The CET offset at that UTC time is +02:00. So output = 2020-10-25 00:01:05 +02:00 (same thing). So `startOfDayUtc` = 2020-10-25 00:01:05 +02:00.

But `fireTime` is 2020-10-25 23:01:06 +01:00 (CET). The UTC of this is 2020-10-25 22:01:06.

Now `secondsAfterStart = (fireTime - startOfDayUtc).TotalSeconds`. But these are DateTimeOffsets with different offsets! `fireTime` = 2020-10-25 23:01:06 +01:00, `startOfDayUtc` = 2020-10-25 00:01:05 +02:00.

The subtraction of DateTimeOffsets accounts for the offset difference. So:
- fireTime UTC = 2020-10-25 22:01:06
- startOfDayUtc UTC = 2020-10-24 22:01:05
- Difference = 24 hours + 1 second = 86401 seconds

Then `jumpCount = secondsAfterStart / (24 * 3600)` = 86401 / 86400 = 1 (integer division). 
`secondsAfterStart % (24 * 3600)` = 86401 % 86400 = 1, which is != 0, so jumpCount++ → jumpCount = 2.

So `sTime = sTime.AddHours(24 * 2)` = 2020-10-24 22:01:05 UTC + 48h = 2020-10-26 22:01:05 UTC.

Then `fireTime = TimeZoneUtil.ConvertTime(sTime, TimeZone)` = Convert 2020-10-26 22:01:05 UTC to CET. Oct 26 is in winter time (CET, +01:00). So output = 2020-10-26 23:01:05 +01:00.

Then we return `fireTime?.ToUniversalTime()` = 2020-10-26 23:01:05 UTC.

But the expected result should be 2020-10-26 23:01:05 UTC (which is 2020-10-27 00:01:05 CET). Wait, actually we got 4 fire times and expected 3. Let me look at the output again:

So the first fire time is wrong: Oct 25 23:01:05 CET instead of Oct 25 00:01:05 CEST. And there's an extra one on Oct 28.

The issue is in `GetFireTimeAfter`. The first call gives the wrong time because:
- The `startTimeUtc` is 2020-10-25 00:01:05 UTC (which is Oct 25 02:01:05 CEST)
- After converting to CET, we get fireTime = 2020-10-25 02:01:05 CEST (after the start time of day 00:01:05)
- The jump count calculation gives jumpCount = 1, so it adds 24 hours to the startOfDay in UTC.
- But adding 24 hours to 2020-10-24 22:01:05 UTC = 2020-10-25 22:01:05 UTC, which converts to 2020-10-25 23:01:05 CET.

But the first fire time should be at 2020-10-25 00:01:05 CEST = 2020-10-24 22:01:05 UTC. The problem is that `afterTime` (02:01:05 CEST) is after `fireTimeStartDate` (00:01:05 CEST), so it tries to find the next interval. With 24-hour interval, the next one after startOfDay would be 24 hours later, which is 2020-10-26 00:01:05 (but since DST changes, it's 2020-10-25 23:01:05 UTC = 2020-10-26 00:01:05 CET). But 2020-10-25 00:01:05 CEST should be THE first fire time, it's just that the trigger's startTimeUtc is set to 2020-10-25 00:01:05 UTC = 2020-10-25 02:01:05 CEST, which is AFTER the startTimeOfDay for that day.

So actually, the PR's scenario has `StartAt` = `startDateTime.AddMinutes(1).AddSeconds(5)` = 2020-10-25 00:01:05 UTC. And `startDateTimeOffset` = 2020-10-25 00:00:00 UTC.

The trigger's StartTimeUtc is 2020-10-25 00:01:05 UTC. And the query range is [2020-10-25 00:00:00 UTC, 2020-10-28 00:00:00 UTC].

Now, `ComputeFireTimesBetween`:
- Since `nextFireTimeUtc` is null, it computes first fire time.
- But before that, it checks if `t.StartTimeUtc < from || t.StartTimeUtc > to`. StartTimeUtc = 2020-10-25 00:01:05 UTC, from = 2020-10-25 00:00:00 UTC. So `StartTimeUtc > from` is true, and StartTimeUtc is NOT changed.

Then `ComputeFirstFireTimeUtc` calls `GetFireTimeAfter(StartTimeUtc.AddSeconds(-1))` = `GetFireTimeAfter(2020-10-25 00:01:04 UTC)`.

In `GetFireTimeAfter`:
- `afterTime` = 2020-10-25 00:01:04 UTC + 1s = 2020-10-25 00:01:05 UTC
- Check: `afterTime < startTimeUtc`? No, it's equal.
- `afterTime = TimeZoneUtil.ConvertTime(2020-10-25 00:01:05 UTC, CET)` = 2020-10-25 02:01:05 CEST.

Now, the startTimeOfDay is 00:01:05. The first fire time on Oct 25 should be 00:01:05 CEST = 2020-10-24 22:01:05 UTC. But since afterTime (02:01:05 CEST) is after startTimeOfDay (00:01:05 CEST), the code computes the next interval after startTimeOfDay.

The issue is that the algorithm converts afterTime to local time, then checks if it's before startTimeOfDay. Since it's after, it computes the next interval jump. With 24-hour interval, the next jump from startTimeOfDay (00:01:05) is 24 hours later = 2020-10-26 00:01:05. But due to DST, 24 hours later from Oct 25 00:01:05 CEST is Oct 26 00:01:05 CET (which is only 23 hours later in UTC).

Actually, the core problem might be simpler. Let me look at the `AddHours(24)` calculation more carefully.

`sTime = fireTimeStartDate.ToUniversalTime()` = 2020-10-24 22:01:05 UTC (since fireTimeStartDate = 2020-10-25 00:01:05 +02:00).

`sTime.AddHours(24)` = 2020-10-25 22:01:05 UTC.

`TimeZoneUtil.ConvertTime(2020-10-25 22:01:05 UTC, CET)` = 2020-10-25 23:01:05 CET (offset +01:00, winter time).

So the algorithm computes the next fire time as Oct 25 23:01:05 CET (which is Oct 26 00:01:05 CET... wait, 23:01:05 + 1 hour = 00:01:05 next day? No, 23:01:05 CET is just 11:01 PM on Oct 25 in CET).

Actually the local time is 23:01:05, not 00:01:05. So the fire time is 23:01:05 local time, which is wrong. The expected fire time should be 00:01:05 local time.

So the bug is: when `AddHours(24)` is done on UTC time, and the DST transition happens, the resulting local time is not 24 hours later in local time but 23 hours later (because the offset changed from +02:00 to +01:00).

The algorithm should be using local time for the interval addition, not UTC time. Let me look at how this is done in the Java Quartz version or see if there's a known fix.

Let me examine the code again more carefully. The key issue is in lines 737-774 of `DailyTimeIntervalTriggerImpl.cs`:

```csharp
DateTimeOffset startOfDayUtc = TimeZoneUtil.ConvertTime(fireTimeStartDate, TimeZone);
long secondsAfterStart = (long) (fireTime.Value - startOfDayUtc).TotalSeconds;
long repeatLong = RepeatInterval;

DateTimeOffset sTime = fireTimeStartDate.ToUniversalTime();
IntervalUnit repeatUnit = RepeatIntervalUnit;
long jumpCount = 0;
if (repeatUnit == IntervalUnit.Second)
{
    jumpCount = secondsAfterStart / repeatLong;
    if (secondsAfterStart % repeatLong != 0)
    {
        jumpCount++;
    }
    sTime = sTime.AddSeconds(RepeatInterval * (int) jumpCount);
    fireTime = TimeZoneUtil.ConvertTime(sTime, TimeZone);
}
else if (repeatUnit == IntervalUnit.Minute)
{
    // ...
}
else if (repeatUnit == IntervalUnit.Hour)
{
    jumpCount = secondsAfterStart / (repeatLong * 60L * 60L);
    if (secondsAfterStart % (repeatLong * 60L * 60L) != 0)
    {
        jumpCount++;
    }
    sTime = sTime.AddHours(RepeatInterval * (int) jumpCount);
    fireTime = TimeZoneUtil.ConvertTime(sTime, TimeZone);
}
```

The problem: `sTime` is computed as UTC time (`fireTimeStartDate.ToUniversalTime()`). Then `AddHours` is done on UTC time. But if there's a DST transition, adding N hours to UTC time does NOT correspond to adding N hours to local time. The result is then converted back to local time via `TimeZoneUtil.ConvertTime`.

The fix should be to do the interval arithmetic in local time, then convert back to UTC. Instead of:
```csharp
sTime = fireTimeStartDate.ToUniversalTime();
sTime = sTime.AddHours(...);
fireTime = TimeZoneUtil.ConvertTime(sTime, TimeZone);
```

It should be something like:
```csharp
fireTime = fireTimeStartDate.AddHours(...);
```

But even that might have issues with DST. Actually, `DateTimeOffset.AddHours` adds exact 60-minute hours regardless of DST. So adding 24 hours to 2020-10-25 00:01:05 +02:00 gives 2020-10-26 00:01:05 +02:00, which is not correct because the actual local time should be 2020-10-26 00:01:05 +01:00 (CET).

Wait, actually `DateTimeOffset.AddHours` preserves the offset, so we'd get the wrong offset. But then when we convert to the target timezone, it should correct it.

Let me think about this differently. The goal is: given a start time of day (00:01:05) in a specific timezone, find the next fire time after a given afterTime, where fire times are at intervals of N hours from the start of day.

The correct approach should be:
1. Determine the start time for the day (in the target timezone)
2. Calculate how many intervals have passed since start of day
3. The next fire time = start of day + (jumpCount * interval) in the target timezone
4. Convert to UTC for the result

The current code does:
1. Determine start time for the day (in target timezone with correct offset)
2. Convert to UTC
3. Add intervals in UTC
4. Convert back to target timezone

This is wrong because the UTC offset changes during DST transitions, so adding in UTC doesn't correspond to adding in local time.

Let me now look at the existing DST tests to see how they handle this:

Looking at `TestDayLightSaving`:
```csharp
var trigger = DailyTimeIntervalScheduleBuilder.Create()
    .StartingDailyAt(TimeOfDay.HourAndMinuteOfDay(22, 15))
    .OnEveryDay()
    .WithIntervalInHours(24)
    .WithRepeatCount(9999)
    .InTimeZone(timeZoneInfo)
    .Build();

var first = trigger.GetFireTimeAfter(new DateTimeOffset(2014, 10, 25, 0, 0, 0, TimeSpan.Zero));
Assert.That(first, Is.EqualTo(new DateTimeOffset(2014, 10, 25, 22, 15, 0, TimeSpan.FromHours(1))));

var second = trigger.GetFireTimeAfter(first);
Assert.That(second, Is.EqualTo(new DateTimeOffset(2014, 10, 26, 22, 15, 0, TimeSpan.FromHours(0))));
```

This test passes! So the DST case with 22:15 start time works correctly. Why does it work for 22:15 but not for 00:01:05?

Let me think... with 22:15 start time:
- On Oct 25, 22:15 BST (British Summer Time, +01:00) = 21:15 UTC
- On Oct 26, 22:15 GMT (+00:00) = 22:15 UTC

The difference between the two UTC times is 25 hours. That's because the clocks go back 1 hour at 2:00 AM BST on Oct 26 (actually Oct 25 at 2:00 AM? No, UK DST ends on the last Sunday of October, which in 2014 was Oct 26).

Wait, for 2014 Oct 26 was the DST change in UK. So:
- Oct 25 22:15 BST = Oct 25 21:15 UTC
- Oct 26 22:15 GMT = Oct 26 22:15 UTC

The difference is 25 hours in UTC. Now let me trace the algorithm for the second call `GetFireTimeAfter(first)` where first = Oct 25 22:15 BST = Oct 25 21:15 UTC:

- `afterTime = first.AddSeconds(1)` = 2020-10-25 21:15:01 UTC
- `afterTime = ConvertTime(..., GMT Standard Time)` = 2020-10-25 22:15:01 BST (+01:00)
- `afterTimePastEndTimeOfDay`: 22:15:01 > 23:59:59? No.
- `AdvanceToNextDayOfWeekIfNecessary`: No advance (every day).
- `fireTimeEndDate` = 2020-10-25 23:59:59 BST
- `fireTimeStartDate` = startTimeOfDay (22:15) on that date with offset from fireTime = 2020-10-25 22:15:00 +01:00
- Apply offset: `TimeZoneUtil.GetUtcOffset(2020-10-25 22:15:00, GMT Standard Time)`. On Oct 25 2020 at 22:15, the UK is still in BST (+01:00). So offset = +01:00.
- `fireTime` (22:15:01 BST) > `fireTimeStartDate` (22:15:00 BST), so compute interval.
- `sTime = fireTimeStartDate.ToUniversalTime()` = 2020-10-25 21:15:00 UTC
- `secondsAfterStart = (fireTime - startOfDayUtc).TotalSeconds` = 1 second
- `jumpCount = 1 / (24*3600)` = 0, remainder != 0, so jumpCount = 1.
- `sTime = sTime.AddHours(24 * 1)` = 2020-10-26 21:15:00 UTC
- `fireTime = ConvertTime(2020-10-26 21:15:00 UTC, GMT Standard Time)` = 2020-10-26 22:15:00 GMT (+00:00)

That works correctly! The UTC time is 21:15, and the local time is 22:15. The interval is 24 local hours, which in UTC is 25 hours due to DST change. Adding 24 hours to UTC (21:15 UTC + 24h = 21:15 UTC next day) coincidentally gives the right local time because the DST change happens at 2:00 AM, and 22:15 is after the DST change on both days.

Now for the failing case with 00:01:05:
- On Oct 25, 00:01:05 CEST (+02:00) = Oct 24 22:01:05 UTC
- On Oct 26, 00:01:05 CET (+01:00) = Oct 25 23:01:05 UTC
- The UTC difference is 25 hours.

Now for the first call `GetFireTimeAfter(startTimeUtc.AddSeconds(-1))`:
- `afterTime` = 2020-10-25 00:01:04 UTC + 1s = 2020-10-25 00:01:05 UTC
- `afterTime = ConvertTime(2020-10-25 00:01:05 UTC, CET)` = 2020-10-25 02:01:05 CEST (+02:00)
- `afterTimePastEndTimeOfDay`: 02:01:05 > 23:59:59? No.
- `AdvanceToNextDayOfWeekIfNecessary`: No advance.
- `fireTimeEndDate` = 2020-10-25 23:59:59 CEST (since fireTime is still in CEST)
- `fireTimeStartDate` = startTimeOfDay (00:01:05) on that date with offset from fireTime = 2020-10-25 00:01:05 +02:00
- Apply offset: `GetUtcOffset(2020-10-25 00:01:05, CET)` = +02:00 (still summer time at 00:01:05)
- `fireTime` (02:01:05 CEST) > `fireTimeStartDate` (00:01:05 CEST), so compute interval.
- `sTime = fireTimeStartDate.ToUniversalTime()` = 2020-10-24 22:01:05 UTC
- `secondsAfterStart = (fireTime - startOfDayUtc).TotalSeconds` = 2 hours = 7200 seconds
- `jumpCount = 7200 / 86400` = 0, remainder != 0, so jumpCount = 1.
- `sTime = sTime.AddHours(24 * 1)` = 2020-10-25 22:01:05 UTC
- `fireTime = ConvertTime(2020-10-25 22:01:05 UTC, CET)` = 2020-10-25 23:01:05 CET (+01:00)

But the expected fire time should be 2020-10-25 00:01:05 CEST = 2020-10-24 22:01:05 UTC.

The problem here is different! The `afterTime` is 02:01:05 CEST, which is after the startTimeOfDay (00:01:05). So the code correctly decides to jump to the next interval. But 00:01:05 + 24 hours = 00:01:05 next day. However, due to DST, 00:01:05 next day in local time = Oct 25 23:01:05 UTC (instead of Oct 26 00:01:05 UTC if there were no DST).

But wait: the `sTime.AddHours(24)` adds 24 hours to UTC time (2020-10-24 22:01:05 UTC + 24h = 2020-10-25 22:01:05 UTC). Converting to CET gives 2020-10-25 23:01:05 CET. But the local time of 2020-10-26 00:01:05 CET = 2020-10-25 23:01:05 UTC. So the result (2020-10-25 22:01:05 UTC) is NOT 2020-10-26 00:01:05 CET. It's 2020-10-25 23:01:05 CET.

So the algorithm produces 23:01:05 instead of 00:01:05. That's because adding 24 hours to UTC doesn't account for the DST change.

But the test `TestDayLightSaving` passes for 22:15... why? Because 22:15 is after the DST change time (2:00 AM). When you convert UTC to local time for Oct 25 22:15 BST, it's after DST change? No, Oct 25 is still BST. The DST change happens at 2:00 AM on Oct 26 (actually Oct 25 for UK? Let me check). 

In the UK, DST ends at 2:00 AM BST on the last Sunday of October, which in 2014 was October 26. So:
- Oct 25 22:15 BST = Oct 25 21:15 UTC (BST is +01:00)
- Oct 26 22:15 GMT = Oct 26 22:15 UTC (GMT is +00:00)

The UTC difference is 25 hours. Now when we add 24 hours to UTC:
- For the first fire time (Oct 25 22:15 BST): `sTime = fireTimeStartDate.ToUniversalTime()` = Oct 25 21:15 UTC. `sTime.AddHours(24)` = Oct 26 21:15 UTC. `ConvertTime(Oct 26 21:15 UTC, GMT)` = Oct 26 22:15 GMT. Correct!

But wait, the UTC time is Oct 26 21:15 UTC, and the local time is Oct 26 22:15 GMT. The offset is +01:00? No, GMT is +00:00. Oct 26 21:15 UTC + 00:00 = Oct 26 21:15 GMT? That's not 22:15.

Let me re-check. `TimeZoneInfo.ConvertTime(DateTimeOffset, TimeZoneInfo)`:

From .NET docs: "Converts the time in a specified DateTimeOffset to a new DateTimeOffset value that represents the same point in time in the destination time zone."

So `ConvertTime(2020-10-26 21:15:00 +00:00, GMT Standard Time)` = the same instant in GMT Standard Time. On Oct 26 at 21:15 UTC, GMT Standard Time is at offset +00:00 (winter time). So the result is 2020-10-26 21:15:00 +00:00. That IS 21:15 GMT, not 22:15.

But the test says `second` should be `new DateTimeOffset(2014, 10, 26, 22, 15, 0, TimeSpan.FromHours(0))`. That's Oct 26 22:15 with offset 0, which is 22:15 UTC.

So the test expects:
- First: Oct 25 22:15 +01:00 = Oct 25 21:15 UTC
- Second: Oct 26 22:15 +00:00 = Oct 26 22:15 UTC

The difference is 25 hours in UTC. But we added only 24 hours to UTC (from 21:15 to 21:15 next day). That would give Oct 26 21:15 UTC = Oct 26 21:15 GMT. That's NOT 22:15.

Wait, I must be confusing the date. Let me check: does the test actually pass?

2026-05-29 09:43:33,674 - INFO - swea-agent - 💭 THOUGHT
The first test (GMT Standard Time) just uses the current time (2026-05-29) which doesn't cross DST. But the test TestDayLightSaving uses 2014 dates. The issue is that the trigger's StartTimeUtc defaults to "now" (TimeProvider.GetUtcNow()) when created.

Now I see the key difference. The 22:15 case works because 22:15 is after the DST transition. The 00:01:05 case fails because 00:01:05 is before the DST transition (which happens at 3:00 AM CEST → 2:00 AM CET).

Let me now understand the actual fix needed. The core issue is in how `GetFireTimeAfter` computes the next fire time. The interval addition is done in UTC, but should be done in local time.

Let me look at the code section again:

```csharp
DateTimeOffset sTime = fireTimeStartDate.ToUniversalTime();
...
sTime = sTime.AddHours(RepeatInterval * (int) jumpCount);
fireTime = TimeZoneUtil.ConvertTime(sTime, TimeZone);
```

This converts the start time to UTC, adds hours in UTC, then converts back. But if DST changes during that interval, the result is wrong.

The fix should add the interval in local time instead:

```csharp
fireTime = fireTimeStartDate.AddHours(RepeatInterval * (int) jumpCount);
// then convert to the target timezone to get correct offset
fireTime = TimeZoneUtil.ConvertTime(fireTime, TimeZone);
```

Wait, but `DateTimeOffset.AddHours` preserves the original offset. So if `fireTimeStartDate` is 2020-10-25 00:01:05 +02:00, adding 24 hours gives 2020-10-26 00:01:05 +02:00. Then converting to CET timezone would give 2020-10-26 00:01:05 +01:00 (since Oct 26 is winter time). Then `.ToUniversalTime()` would give 2020-10-25 23:01:05 UTC. That's correct!

But wait, there's also the issue with `AddSeconds` and `AddMinutes` for the other interval types. They have the same issue.

Let me also look at the `secondsAfterStart` calculation:

```csharp
long secondsAfterStart = (long) (fireTime.Value - startOfDayUtc).TotalSeconds;
```

Where `startOfDayUtc = TimeZoneUtil.ConvertTime(fireTimeStartDate, TimeZone)`.

This calculates the difference between two DateTimeOffset values (which accounts for different offsets). So `secondsAfterStart` should be the actual elapsed time in seconds since start of day. That seems correct.

But wait, `startOfDayUtc` might not be the actual start of day in the target timezone. Let me trace:

- `fireTimeStartDate = startTimeOfDay.GetTimeOfDayForDate(fireTime.Value)` — this uses the offset from fireTime
- Then `fireTimeStartDate = new DateTimeOffset(fireTimeStartDate.DateTime, TimeZoneUtil.GetUtcOffset(fireTimeStartDate.DateTime, TimeZone))` — this applies the correct offset for that local time

For the failing case:
- `fireTime.Value` = 2020-10-25 02:01:05 +02:00 (CEST)
- `fireTimeStartDate` = 2020-10-25 00:01:05 +02:00 (using fireTime's offset)
- `GetUtcOffset(2020-10-25 00:01:05, CET)` = +02:00 (still DST at midnight)
- So `fireTimeStartDate` stays 2020-10-25 00:01:05 +02:00
- `startOfDayUtc = ConvertTime(fireTimeStartDate, TimeZone)` = 2020-10-25 00:01:05 +02:00
- `secondsAfterStart = (fireTime - startOfDayUtc).TotalSeconds` = (02:01:05+02:00 - 00:01:05+02:00) = 2 hours = 7200 seconds
- `jumpCount = 7200 / 86400 = 0`, remainder != 0, so jumpCount = 1
- `sTime = fireTimeStartDate.ToUniversalTime()` = 2020-10-24 22:01:05 UTC
- `sTime.AddHours(24)` = 2020-10-25 22:01:05 UTC
- `ConvertTime(2020-10-25 22:01:05 UTC, CET)` = 2020-10-25 23:01:05 CET (+01:00)

But the expected:
- fireTimeStartDate = 2020-10-25 00:01:05 +02:00
- Add 24 hours in local time: 2020-10-26 00:01:05 +02:00 (preserving offset)
- Convert to target timezone: 2020-10-26 00:01:05 +01:00 (winter time)
- ToUniversalTime: 2020-10-25 23:01:05 UTC

But wait, the expected first fire time should be at 00:01:05 local time on Oct 25, which is 2020-10-24 22:01:05 UTC. The code produces 2020-10-25 22:01:05 UTC = 2020-10-25 23:01:05 CET.

The problem is that `afterTime` (02:01:05 CEST) is AFTER the startTimeOfDay (00:01:05 CEST), so it thinks the first fire time has passed and jumps to the next one. But actually, the first fire time on Oct 25 at 00:01:05 CEST hasn't occurred yet — or has it?

The trigger's StartTimeUtc is set to 2020-10-25 00:01:05 UTC = 2020-10-25 02:01:05 CEST. And the query range starts at 2020-10-25 00:00:00 UTC = 2020-10-25 02:00:00 CEST.

The first fire time for that day (00:01:05 CEST = 2020-10-24 22:01:05 UTC) is BEFORE the trigger's StartTimeUtc AND before the query range. So it should be skipped.

But then the next fire time should be 00:01:05 on Oct 26 = 2020-10-25 23:01:05 UTC (due to DST). That's what the algorithm produces as the second result. But it also produces an extra result at 2020-10-25 22:01:05 UTC = 2020-10-25 23:01:05 CET, which is wrong because it's not 00:01:05 local time.

So there are actually two issues:
1. The first fire time is wrong (23:01:05 instead of 00:01:05 next day)
2. There's an extra fire time because of the wrong calculation

Both issues stem from the same root cause: the interval arithmetic is done in UTC instead of local time.

Let me fix the `GetFireTimeAfter` method. The key change is to do the interval addition in local time and then convert to the target timezone for proper offset handling.

Actually, looking again, for the hour case:

```csharp
sTime = sTime.AddHours(RepeatInterval * (int) jumpCount);
fireTime = TimeZoneUtil.ConvertTime(sTime, TimeZone);
```

Instead, we should do:

```csharp
fireTime = fireTimeStartDate.AddHours(RepeatInterval * (int) jumpCount);
fireTime = TimeZoneUtil.ConvertTime(fireTime, TimeZone);
```

Similarly for minutes and seconds.

But there's a subtlety: `fireTimeStartDate` has the correct offset for the start of the day (as determined by `GetUtcOffset` on the DateTime). When we add hours to it, `DateTimeOffset.AddHours` preserves the offset. But the DST might change during the interval, so we need to re-convert with `TimeZoneUtil.ConvertTime` to get the correct offset.

Let me check if this fix would break the working test case (22:15):

- `fireTimeStartDate` = 2020-10-25 22:15:00 +01:00 (BST)
- With the fix: `fireTimeStartDate.AddHours(24)` = 2020-10-26 22:15:00 +01:00
- `TimeZoneUtil.ConvertTime(2020-10-26 22:15:00 +01:00, GMT Standard Time)` = ? 

The UTC time of the input is 2020-10-26 21:15:00 UTC. The GMT Standard Time offset at that UTC time is +00:00 (winter). So the output is 2020-10-26 21:15:00 +00:00 = 2020-10-26 21:15 GMT. But the expected is 2020-10-26 22:15 GMT!

So this fix would BREAK the working case! Why?

Because `fireTimeStartDate.AddHours(24)` adds 24 hours to the local time, giving 22:15 on the next day. But the UTC time of that result is 2020-10-26 21:15 (since offset is still +01:00). Converting to the target timezone (GMT) at that UTC instant gives offset +00:00, so the result is 21:15 GMT, not 22:15 GMT.

The issue is that we need the local time to be 22:15, not 21:15. Adding 24 hours to Oct 25 22:15 BST should give Oct 26 22:15 GMT. But `DateTimeOffset.AddHours(24)` gives Oct 26 22:15 with the SAME offset (+01:00), which is incorrect because on Oct 26, the offset is +00:00.

So we need a different approach. Let me think...

The correct approach for adding hours in a DST-aware way:
1. Get the local time in the target timezone
2. Add the interval to the local DateTime (not DateTimeOffset) 
3. Convert back to DateTimeOffset with the correct offset for that resulting local time

But we need to handle ambiguous times (when clocks go back) and invalid times (when clocks go forward).

Actually, looking at how Java Quartz handles this, they use `Calendar` with the timezone set, and `Calendar.add(Calendar.HOUR_OF_DAY, hours)` automatically handles DST transitions.

For .NET, the approach should be:
1. Convert `fireTimeStartDate` to the target timezone (which it already is)
2. Get the DateTime (local time without offset)
3. Add the interval to the DateTime
4. Get the UTC offset for that new DateTime in the target timezone
5. Create a DateTimeOffset with the new DateTime and the new offset

Something like:

```csharp
DateTime localDateTime = fireTimeStartDate.DateTime;
localDateTime = localDateTime.AddHours(RepeatInterval * (int) jumpCount);
TimeSpan newOffset = TimeZoneUtil.GetUtcOffset(localDateTime, TimeZone);
fireTime = new DateTimeOffset(localDateTime, newOffset);
```

Let me verify this with the two cases:

**Case 1 (22:15 BST):**
- `fireTimeStartDate` = 2020-10-25 22:15:00 +01:00
- `localDateTime` = 2020-10-25 22:15:00
- `localDateTime.AddHours(24)` = 2020-10-26 22:15:00
- `GetUtcOffset(2020-10-26 22:15:00, GMT Standard Time)` = +00:00 (winter time, and not ambiguous)
- `new DateTimeOffset(2020-10-26 22:15:00, +00:00)` = 2020-10-26 22:15:00 +00:00 = 22:15 GMT ✓

**Case 2 (00:01:05 CET):**
- `fireTimeStartDate` = 2020-10-25 00:01:05 +02:00
- `localDateTime` = 2020-10-25 00:01:05
- `localDateTime.AddHours(24)` = 2020-10-26 00:01:05
- `GetUtcOffset(2020-10-26 00:01:05, CET)` = +01:00 (winter time, not ambiguous)
- `new DateTimeOffset(2020-10-26 00:01:05, +01:00)` = 2020-10-26 00:01:05 +01:00 = 2020-10-25 23:01:05 UTC ✓

Now let me also verify with the spring-forward DST case (e.g., March 29, 2020 for CET):

**Case 3 (spring forward, 02:30 CET):**
On March 29, 2020, clocks go forward from 2:00 AM to 3:00 AM, so 02:30 doesn't exist.
- `fireTimeStartDate` = 2020-03-29 00:01:05 +01:00
- `localDateTime` = 2020-03-29 00:01:05
- `localDateTime.AddHours(24)` = 2020-03-30 00:01:05
- `GetUtcOffset(2020-03-30 00:01:05, CET)` = +02:00 (summer time)
- `new DateTimeOffset(2020-03-30 00:01:05, +02:00)` = 2020-03-29 22:01:05 UTC

But what if the interval causes us to land on an invalid time? E.g., if startTimeOfDay = 02:30 and we add 0 hours (jumpCount = 0)?

Actually, `GetUtcOffset` handles this via `TimeZoneInfo.GetUtcOffset(DateTime)` which will throw for invalid times. But in our case, we always start from a valid time (startTimeOfDay which is 00:01:05, a valid time). Adding multiples of hours (like 24) always lands on the same time of day, which is valid.

But what about intervals that aren't multiples of 24 hours? For example, if the interval is 12 hours, the fire times could be 00:01:05 and 12:01:05. Both are valid.

What about if the interval causes the fire time to land on the "skipped" hour during spring forward? E.g., startTimeOfDay = 01:00, interval = 1 hour. On spring forward day, 02:00 and 02:xx don't exist. But our algorithm would try to create a DateTimeOffset for 02:00 with the corresponding offset, which would be invalid. However, `TimeZoneInfo.GetUtcOffset` throws for invalid times.

But this is an edge case that's probably already handled (or not) in the current code. The PR issue is specifically about the fall-back DST transition.

Now let me implement the fix. But I need to be careful: the `secondsAfterStart` calculation also needs to be fixed. Currently:

```csharp
long secondsAfterStart = (long) (fireTime.Value - startOfDayUtc).TotalSeconds;
```

This calculates the difference between two DateTimeOffset values. Since they might have different offsets, this correctly gives the elapsed seconds. However, if we're going to use local time for the jump calculation, we should also use local time for `secondsAfterStart`.

Actually, `secondsAfterStart` should be the number of seconds between the start of day (in local time) and the current fireTime (in local time). Since both are in the same timezone, we can just compare their local times:

Actually, the current calculation works because DateTimeOffset subtraction accounts for offset differences. But let me verify: if `fireTime` = 2020-10-25 23:01:06 +01:00 and `startOfDayUtc` = 2020-10-25 00:01:05 +02:00:
- fireTime UTC = 2020-10-25 22:01:06
- startOfDayUtc UTC = 2020-10-24 22:01:05
- Difference = 86401 seconds ✓

That's correct because the actual elapsed local time is 23:01:06 - 00:01:05 = 23 hours = 82800 seconds? No, local time 23:01:06 - 00:01:05 = 23:00:01 = 82801 seconds. But the UTC difference is 86401 seconds, which is 1 hour more because of DST (the day has 25 hours).

Hmm, which one is correct for the jump calculation? The jump calculation should determine how many intervals have passed since start of day. If the interval is 24 hours, then after 23 local hours, 0 full intervals have passed. After 24 local hours, 1 full interval has passed. But the UTC difference of 86401 seconds = 24 hours + 1 second. So jumpCount = 86401 / 86400 = 1. But in local time, only 23 hours have passed, so 0 intervals should have passed.

Wait, this is confusing. Let me re-think.

The `secondsAfterStart` should represent the elapsed time since start of day. If we want to compute "how many 24-hour intervals have elapsed since start of day," we should use local time. But the UTC-based calculation gives the wrong answer when DST changes because the day doesn't have exactly 24 hours.

Actually, the issue is more fundamental. The current code computes `secondsAfterStart` as the real elapsed seconds (UTC difference). If the day has 25 hours due to DST fall-back, then the elapsed UTC seconds from 00:01:05 CEST to 23:01:06 CET is 25 hours + 1 second. The jumpCount = ceil(25h+1s / 24h) = 2, meaning 2 intervals have passed. But in local time, only 23 hours have passed, which is less than 1 interval.

The correct approach is to compute the difference in local time (wall clock time), not UTC time.

Let me now prepare the fix:

For all three interval types (hour, minute, second), the fix should:
1. Compute `secondsAfterStart` based on local time difference (or just use the local DateTime values)
2. Add the interval in local time using `DateTime.AddHours/AddMinutes/AddSeconds` 
3. Then create a new DateTimeOffset with the correct offset for the resulting local time

The key changes needed:

1. **`secondsAfterStart` calculation**: Currently uses UTC difference, should use local time difference. Change from:
   ```csharp
   DateTimeOffset startOfDayUtc = TimeZoneUtil.ConvertTime(fireTimeStartDate, TimeZone);
   long secondsAfterStart = (long) (fireTime.Value - startOfDayUtc).TotalSeconds;
   ```
   to:
   ```csharp
   long secondsAfterStart = (long) (fireTime.Value.DateTime - fireTimeStartDate.DateTime).TotalSeconds;
   ```

2. **Interval addition**: Currently converts to UTC, adds interval, converts back. Should add interval in local time and then determine the correct offset. Change from:
   ```csharp
   DateTimeOffset sTime = fireTimeStartDate.ToUniversalTime();
   ...
   sTime = sTime.AddSeconds/AddMinutes/AddHours(...);
   fireTime = TimeZoneUtil.ConvertTime(sTime, TimeZone);
   ```
   to:
   ```csharp
   DateTime localFireTime = fireTimeStartDate.DateTime;
   ...
   localFireTime = localFireTime.AddSeconds/AddMinutes/AddHours(...);
   fireTime = new DateTimeOffset(localFireTime, TimeZoneUtil.GetUtcOffset(localFireTime, TimeZone));
   ```

Step h: `if (fireTime > fireTimeEndDate)` — this compares DateTimeOffset values. Since both have correct offsets for their respective local times, the comparison should work correctly.



`fireTime.Value.DateTime` and `fireTimeStartDate.DateTime` both strip the offset. The difference is the wall clock difference, which is what we want for determining how many intervals have passed.

For the failing case:
- `fireTime.Value.DateTime` = 2020-10-25 02:01:05
- `fireTimeStartDate.DateTime` = 2020-10-25 00:01:05
- Difference = 2 hours = 7200 seconds
- `jumpCount = 7200 / 86400 = 0`, remainder != 0, so jumpCount = 1

With the fix, the new `fireTime` would be:
- `fireTimeStartDate.DateTime.AddHours(24 * 1)` = 2020-10-26 00:01:05
- `new DateTimeOffset(2020-10-26 00:01:05, GetUtcOffset(2020-10-26 00:01:05, CET))` = 2020-10-26 00:01:05 +01:00
- `.ToUniversalTime()` = 2020-10-25 23:01:05 UTC ✓

Now for the second call (after the first correct fire time):
- `afterTime` = 2020-10-25 23:01:05 UTC + 1s = 2020-10-25 23:01:06 UTC
- `ConvertTime(..., CET)` = 2020-10-26 00:01:06 CET (+01:00)
- `fireTimeStartDate` = 2020-10-26 00:01:05 +01:00
- `fireTime` (00:01:06) > `fireTimeStartDate` (00:01:05), so compute interval
- `secondsAfterStart = (00:01:06 - 00:01:05) = 1 second`
- `jumpCount = 1 / 86400 = 0`, remainder != 0, so jumpCount = 1
- `localFireTime = 2020-10-26 00:01:05.AddHours(24)` = 2020-10-27 00:01:05
- `new DateTimeOffset(2020-10-27 00:01:05, GetUtcOffset(2020-10-27 00:01:05, CET))` = 2020-10-27 00:01:05 +01:00
- `.ToUniversalTime()` = 2020-10-26 23:01:05 UTC ✓

import sys
with open('src/Quartz/Impl/Triggers/DailyTimeIntervalTriggerImpl.cs', 'r') as f:
    content = f.read()

old = '''        // f. Continue to calculate the fireTime by incremental unit of intervals.
        // recall that if fireTime was less that fireTimeStartDate, we didn't get this far
        DateTimeOffset startOfDayUtc = TimeZoneUtil.ConvertTime(fireTimeStartDate, TimeZone);
        long secondsAfterStart = (long) (fireTime.Value - startOfDayUtc).TotalSeconds;
        long repeatLong = RepeatInterval;

        DateTimeOffset sTime = fireTimeStartDate.ToUniversalTime();
        IntervalUnit repeatUnit = RepeatIntervalUnit;
        long jumpCount = 0;
        if (repeatUnit == IntervalUnit.Second)
        {
            jumpCount = secondsAfterStart / repeatLong;
            if (secondsAfterStart % repeatLong != 0)
            {
                jumpCount++;
            }

            sTime = sTime.AddSeconds(RepeatInterval * (int) jumpCount);
            fireTime = TimeZoneUtil.ConvertTime(sTime, TimeZone);
        }
        else if (repeatUnit == IntervalUnit.Minute)
        {
            jumpCount = secondsAfterStart / (repeatLong * 60L);
            if (secondsAfterStart % (repeatLong * 60L) != 0)
            {
                jumpCount++;
            }
            sTime = sTime.AddMinutes(RepeatInterval * (int) jumpCount);
            fireTime = TimeZoneUtil.ConvertTime(sTime, TimeZone);
        }
        else if (repeatUnit == IntervalUnit.Hour)
        {
            jumpCount = secondsAfterStart / (repeatLong * 60L * 60L);
            if (secondsAfterStart % (repeatLong * 60L * 60L) != 0)
            {
                jumpCount++;
            }
            sTime = sTime.AddHours(RepeatInterval * (int) jumpCount);
            fireTime = TimeZoneUtil.ConvertTime(sTime, TimeZone);
        }'''

new = '''        // f. Continue to calculate the fireTime by incremental unit of intervals.
        // recall that if fireTime was less that fireTimeStartDate, we didn't get this far
        // Use local time difference (wall clock) to correctly handle DST transitions
        long secondsAfterStart = (long) (fireTime.Value.DateTime - fireTimeStartDate.DateTime).TotalSeconds;
        long repeatLong = RepeatInterval;

        DateTime localFireTime = fireTimeStartDate.DateTime;
        IntervalUnit repeatUnit = RepeatIntervalUnit;
        long jumpCount = 0;
        if (repeatUnit == IntervalUnit.Second)
        {
            jumpCount = secondsAfterStart / repeatLong;
            if (secondsAfterStart % repeatLong != 0)
            {
                jumpCount++;
            }

            localFireTime = localFireTime.AddSeconds(RepeatInterval * (int) jumpCount);
        }
        else if (repeatUnit == IntervalUnit.Minute)
        {
            jumpCount = secondsAfterStart / (repeatLong * 60L);
            if (secondsAfterStart % (repeatLong * 60L) != 0)
            {
                jumpCount++;
            }
            localFireTime = localFireTime.AddMinutes(RepeatInterval * (int) jumpCount);
        }
        else if (repeatUnit == IntervalUnit.Hour)
        {
            jumpCount = secondsAfterStart / (repeatLong * 60L * 60L);
            if (secondsAfterStart % (repeatLong * 60L * 60L) != 0)
            {
                jumpCount++;
            }
            localFireTime = localFireTime.AddHours(RepeatInterval * (int) jumpCount);
        }

        // apply the proper offset for the new local fire time, handling DST transitions
        fireTime = new DateTimeOffset(localFireTime, TimeZoneUtil.GetUtcOffset(localFireTime, TimeZone));'''

if old in content:
    content = content.replace(old, new)

        f.write(content)

else:

            sTime = sTime.AddMinutes(RepeatInterval * (int) jumpCount);
            fireTime = TimeZoneUtil.ConvertTime(sTime, TimeZone);
        }
        else if (repeatUnit == IntervalUnit.Hour)
        {
            jumpCount = secondsAfterStart / (repeatLong * 60L * 60L);
            if (secondsAfterStart % (repeatLong * 60L * 60L) != 0)
            {
                jumpCount++;
            }
            sTime = sTime.AddHours(RepeatInterval * (int) jumpCount);
            fireTime = TimeZoneUtil.ConvertTime(sTime, TimeZone);
        }";

string replacement = @"        // f. Continue to calculate the fireTime by incremental unit of intervals.
        // recall that if fireTime was less that fireTimeStartDate, we didn't get this far
        // Use local time difference (wall clock) to correctly handle DST transitions
        long secondsAfterStart = (long) (fireTime.Value.DateTime - fireTimeStartDate.DateTime).TotalSeconds;
        long repeatLong = RepeatInterval;

        DateTime localFireTime = fireTimeStartDate.DateTime;
        IntervalUnit repeatUnit = RepeatIntervalUnit;
        long jumpCount = 0;
        if (repeatUnit == IntervalUnit.Second)
        {
            jumpCount = secondsAfterStart / repeatLong;
            if (secondsAfterStart % repeatLong != 0)
            {
                jumpCount++;
            }

            localFireTime = localFireTime.AddSeconds(RepeatInterval * (int) jumpCount);
        }
        else if (repeatUnit == IntervalUnit.Minute)
        {
            jumpCount = secondsAfterStart / (repeatLong * 60L);
            if (secondsAfterStart % (repeatLong * 60L) != 0)
            {
                jumpCount++;
            }
            localFireTime = localFireTime.AddMinutes(RepeatInterval * (int) jumpCount);
        }
        else if (repeatUnit == IntervalUnit.Hour)
        {
            jumpCount = secondsAfterStart / (repeatLong * 60L * 60L);
            if (secondsAfterStart % (repeatLong * 60L * 60L) != 0)
            {
                jumpCount++;
            }
            localFireTime = localFireTime.AddHours(RepeatInterval * (int) jumpCount);
        }

        // apply the proper offset for the new local fire time, handling DST transitions
        fireTime = new DateTimeOffset(localFireTime, TimeZoneUtil.GetUtcOffset(localFireTime, TimeZone));";

if (content.Contains(old))
{
    content = content.Replace(old, replacement);
    File.WriteAllText(filePath, content);
    Console.WriteLine("Success: replaced");
}
else
{
    Console.WriteLine("Not found");
    // Show the relevant section
    int idx = content.IndexOf("// f. Continue to calculate");
    if (idx >= 0)
    {
        Console.WriteLine(content.Substring(idx, Math.Min(1500, content.Length - idx)));
    }
}

2026-05-29 09:46:42,257 - DEBUG - swea-lm - Response: ModelResponse(id='42559a37220c4353a465879df683f4d6', created=1780047971, model='DeepSeek-V4-Pro', object='chat.completion', system_fingerprint=None, choices=[Choices(finish_reason='tool_calls', index=0, message=Message(content='We went from 4 wrong fire times to 3 correct fire times (well, the first one is missing Oct 25 but that\'s expected since StartTimeUtc is after startTimeOfDay on Oct 25). But wait, we now have 4 fire times all correct: Oct 26, 27, 28, 29 at 00:01:05 CET. But the PR expected only 3: Oct 25, 26, 27.\n\nThe issue is that the PR\'s trigger has `StartAt` at 2020-10-25 00:01:05 UTC, which is 02:01:05 CEST. The startTimeOfDay is 00:01:05. So the first fire time on Oct 25 at 00:01:05 CEST has already passed. The expected behavior (according to the PR) is that the fire times should be:\n- Oct 25 00:01:05 CEST\n- Oct 26 00:01:05 CET\n- Oct 27 00:01:05 CET\n\nBut that doesn\'t make sense because Oct 25 00:01:05 CEST is before the StartTimeUtc of 02:01:05 CEST. So the trigger shouldn\'t fire at that time.\n\nWait, let me re-read the PR:\n\n```\nTriggerBuilder triggerBuilder = TriggerBuilder.Create()\n    .WithIdentity("id")\n    .ForJob("job")\n    .StartAt(new DateTimeOffset(startDateTime.AddMinutes(1).AddSeconds(5)))\n    .WithDailyTimeIntervalSchedule(...)\n```\n\nWhere `startDateTime = new DateTime(2020, 10, 25)`. So `StartAt` = 2020-10-25 00:01:05. But what offset? `new DateTimeOffset(startDateTime.AddMinutes(1).AddSeconds(5))` creates a DateTimeOffset with the local timezone offset.
