We went from 4 wrong fire times to 3 correct fire times (well, the first one is missing Oct 25 but that's expected since StartTimeUtc is after startTimeOfDay on Oct 25). But wait, we now have 4 fire times all correct: Oct 26, 27, 28, 29 at 00:01:05 CET. But the PR expected only 3: Oct 25, 26, 27.

The issue is that the PR's trigger has `StartAt` at 2020-10-25 00:01:05 UTC, which is 02:01:05 CEST. The startTimeOfDay is 00:01:05. So the first fire time on Oct 25 at 00:01:05 CEST has already passed. The expected behavior (according to the PR) is that the fire times should be:
- Oct 25 00:01:05 CEST
- Oct 26 00:01:05 CET
- Oct 27 00:01:05 CET

But that doesn't make sense because Oct 25 00:01:05 CEST is before the StartTimeUtc of 02:01:05 CEST. So the trigger shouldn't fire at that time.

Wait, let me re-read the PR:

```
TriggerBuilder triggerBuilder = TriggerBuilder.Create()
    .WithIdentity("id")
    .ForJob("job")
    .StartAt(new DateTimeOffset(startDateTime.AddMinutes(1).AddSeconds(5)))
    .WithDailyTimeIntervalSchedule(...)
```

Where `startDateTime = new DateTime(2020, 10, 25)`. So `StartAt` = 2020-10-25 00:01:05. But what offset? `new DateTimeOffset(startDateTime.AddMinutes(1).AddSeconds(5))` creates a DateTimeOffset with the local timezone offset. The PR reporter is likely in a timezone where the offset on Oct 25, 2020 is +02:00 (CEST) or +01:00 (CET)?

Actually, `new DateTime(2020, 10, 25)` creates a DateTime with Kind = Unspecified. `.AddMinutes(1).AddSeconds(5)` gives `2020-10-25 00:01:05`. Then `new DateTimeOffset(date)` uses the local timezone's offset for that local time. If the machine is in CET/CEST, Oct 25 00:01:05 would be CEST (+02:00) since DST ends at 3:00 AM. So StartAt = 2020-10-25 00:01:05 +02:00 = 2020-10-24 22:01:05 UTC.

Then `startDateTimeOffset = new DateTimeOffset(startDateTime)` = 2020-10-25 00:00:00 +02:00 = 2020-10-24 22:00:00 UTC.

The query range is [2020-10-24 22:00:00 UTC, 2020-10-28 22:00:00 UTC] (3 days later).

So the expected fire times are:
- Oct 25 00:01:05 CEST = 2020-10-24 22:01:05 UTC
- Oct 26 00:01:05 CET = 2020-10-25 23:01:05 UTC
- Oct 27 00:01:05 CET = 2020-10-26 23:01:05 UTC

And the extra wrong fire time was:
- Oct 25 23:01:05 CET = 2020-10-25 22:01:05 UTC

Now let me modify my reproduction to match the PR exactly (using the local timezone approach):

cat > /tmp/test_repro/Program.cs << 'ENDOFPROGRAM'
using System;
using System.Collections.Generic;
using System.Linq;
using Quartz;
using Quartz.Impl.Triggers;
using Quartz.Spi;
using Quartz.Util;

// Simulate what the PR reporter experiences: 
// The local timezone is CET/CEST, and the DST transition is Oct 25, 2020
var tz = TimeZoneUtil.FindTimeZoneById("Central European Standard Time");

// Reproduce EXACTLY as in the PR
DateTime startDateTime = new DateTime(2020, 10, 25);
// In the PR, the user is in a timezone where Oct 25 has DST transition
// new DateTimeOffset(dateTime) uses local timezone
// Let's simulate being in CET timezone by constructing the DateTimeOffset with the correct offset
var offsetForOct25 = tz.GetUtcOffset(startDateTime);
DateTimeOffset startDateTimeOffset = new DateTimeOffset(startDateTime, offsetForOct25);
int daysAhead = 3;

// The PR's start time:
DateTime startDateTimeLocal = startDateTime.AddMinutes(1).AddSeconds(5); // Oct 25 00:01:05
var startAtOffset = tz.GetUtcOffset(startDateTimeLocal);
DateTimeOffset startAt = new DateTimeOffset(startDateTimeLocal, startAtOffset);

Console.WriteLine($"startDateTimeOffset: {startDateTimeOffset} (UTC: {startDateTimeOffset.UtcDateTime})");
Console.WriteLine($"startAt: {startAt} (UTC: {startAt.UtcDateTime})");
Console.WriteLine($"Query range: [{startDateTimeOffset}, {startDateTimeOffset.AddDays(daysAhead)})");

TriggerBuilder triggerBuilder = TriggerBuilder.Create()
    .WithIdentity("id")
    .ForJob("job")
    .StartAt(startAt)
    .WithDailyTimeIntervalSchedule(
        scheduleBuilder =>
        {
            scheduleBuilder.OnEveryDay().WithIntervalInHours(24);
            scheduleBuilder
                .StartingDailyAt(new TimeOfDay(0, 1, 5))
                .EndingDailyAt(new TimeOfDay(23, 59, 59))
                .WithMisfireHandlingInstructionDoNothing();
        });

var trigger = (IOperableTrigger)triggerBuilder.Build();
// Set the timezone explicitly
if (trigger is DailyTimeIntervalTriggerImpl dailyTrigger)
{
    dailyTrigger.TimeZone = tz;
}

Console.WriteLine($"Trigger StartTimeUtc: {trigger.StartTimeUtc}");
Console.WriteLine($"Trigger StartTimeUtc in TZ: {TimeZoneInfo.ConvertTime(trigger.StartTimeUtc, tz)}");

IReadOnlyList<DateTimeOffset> fireTimes =
    TriggerUtils.ComputeFireTimesBetween(
    trigger,
    null,
    startDateTimeOffset,
    startDateTimeOffset.AddDays(daysAhead));

Console.WriteLine($"\nNumber of fire times: {fireTimes.Count}");
for (int i = 0; i < fireTimes.Count; i++)
{
    var ft = fireTimes[i];
    var local = TimeZoneInfo.ConvertTime(ft, tz);
    Console.WriteLine($"  [{i}]: {ft} -> UTC: {ft.UtcDateTime}, TZ local: {local}");
}

Console.WriteLine();

// Expected:
// Oct 25 00:01:05 CEST = Oct 24 22:01:05 UTC
// Oct 26 00:01:05 CET = Oct 25 23:01:05 UTC
// Oct 27 00:01:05 CET = Oct 26 23:01:05 UTC
var expected0 = new DateTimeOffset(new DateTime(2020, 10, 25, 0, 1, 5), tz.GetUtcOffset(new DateTime(2020, 10, 25, 0, 1, 5)));
var expected1 = new DateTimeOffset(new DateTime(2020, 10, 26, 0, 1, 5), tz.GetUtcOffset(new DateTime(2020, 10, 26, 0, 1, 5)));
var expected2 = new DateTimeOffset(new DateTime(2020, 10, 27, 0, 1, 5), tz.GetUtcOffset(new DateTime(2020, 10, 27, 0, 1, 5)));

Console.WriteLine($"Expected[0]: {expected0} (UTC: {expected0.UtcDateTime})");
Console.WriteLine($"Expected[1]: {expected1} (UTC: {expected1.UtcDateTime})");
Console.WriteLine($"Expected[2]: {expected2} (UTC: {expected2.UtcDateTime})");

if (fireTimes.Count == 3)
{
    bool ok0 = fireTimes[0] == expected0;
    bool ok1 = fireTimes[1] == expected1;
    bool ok2 = fireTimes[2] == expected2;
    Console.WriteLine($"\nMatches: [0]={ok0}, [1]={ok1}, [2]={ok2}");
    if (ok0 && ok1 && ok2)
        Console.WriteLine("PASS");
    else
        Console.WriteLine("FAIL");
}
else
{
    Console.WriteLine($"FAIL: Expected 3 fire times, got {fireTimes.Count}");
}
ENDOFPROGRAM

Now let me think about edge cases:

1. **Spring-forward DST (clocks go forward)**: For example, on March 29, 2020, CET goes from +01:00 to +02:00 at 2:00 AM (02:00 becomes 03:00). If the startTimeOfDay is 00:01:05, adding 24 hours should give March 30 00:01:05 CEST. Let me verify.

2. **Ambiguous times during fall-back**: When clocks go back, the time from 2:00 AM to 3:00 AM occurs twice. `GetUtcOffset` currently returns the MAX offset (daylight time) for ambiguous times. This means it picks the earlier occurrence. Let me verify this is consistent.

3. **Interval not dividing 24 hours**: Like the 72-minute interval in the test. Let me verify this still works.

Let me write a quick test for these edge cases:

cat > /tmp/test_repro/Program.cs << 'ENDOFPROGRAM'
using System;
using System.Collections.Generic;
using System.Linq;
using Quartz;
using Quartz.Impl.Triggers;
using Quartz.Spi;
using Quartz.Util;

Console.WriteLine("=== Edge Case Tests ===");

// Test 1: Spring-forward DST (March 2020, CET)
Console.WriteLine("\n--- Test 1: Spring Forward DST ---");
var tz = TimeZoneUtil.FindTimeZoneById("Central European Standard Time");

var trigger = DailyTimeIntervalScheduleBuilder.Create()
    .StartingDailyAt(TimeOfDay.HourMinuteAndSecondOfDay(0, 1, 5))
    .OnEveryDay()
    .WithIntervalInHours(24)
    .WithRepeatCount(9999)
    .InTimeZone(tz)
    .Build();

// Set start time to just before DST change
trigger.StartTimeUtc = new DateTimeOffset(2020, 3, 28, 23, 1, 5, TimeSpan.Zero); // March 29 00:01:05 CET = March 28 23:01:05 UTC

var f1 = trigger.GetFireTimeAfter(trigger.StartTimeUtc.AddSeconds(-1));
Console.WriteLine($"FireTime 1: {f1} UTC={f1?.UtcDateTime}, TZ={TimeZoneInfo.ConvertTime(f1.Value, tz)}");
// Expected: March 29 00:01:05 CET = March 28 23:01:05 UTC

var f2 = trigger.GetFireTimeAfter(f1);
Console.WriteLine($"FireTime 2: {f2} UTC={f2?.UtcDateTime}, TZ={TimeZoneInfo.ConvertTime(f2.Value, tz)}");
// Expected: March 30 00:01:05 CEST = March 29 22:01:05 UTC

var f3 = trigger.GetFireTimeAfter(f2);
Console.WriteLine($"FireTime 3: {f3} UTC={f3?.UtcDateTime}, TZ={TimeZoneInfo.ConvertTime(f3.Value, tz)}");
// Expected: March 31 00:01:05 CEST = March 30 22:01:05 UTC

// Test 2: Non-24-hour interval crossing DST
Console.WriteLine("\n--- Test 2: 72-minute interval crossing DST fall-back ---");
var trigger2 = DailyTimeIntervalScheduleBuilder.Create()
    .StartingDailyAt(TimeOfDay.HourMinuteAndSecondOfDay(0, 0, 0))
    .EndingDailyAt(TimeOfDay.HourMinuteAndSecondOfDay(3, 0, 0))
    .OnEveryDay()
    .WithIntervalInMinutes(72)
    .InTimeZone(tz)
    .Build();

trigger2.StartTimeUtc = new DateTimeOffset(2020, 10, 24, 22, 0, 0, TimeSpan.Zero); // Oct 25 00:00:00 CEST

var times = TriggerUtils.ComputeFireTimes((IOperableTrigger)trigger2, null, 10);
Console.WriteLine($"Got {times.Count} fire times:");
foreach (var t in times)
{
    var local = TimeZoneInfo.ConvertTime(t, tz);
    Console.WriteLine($"  {t} -> UTC={t.UtcDateTime}, TZ local={local}");
}
// With start 00:00, interval 72 min = 1h12min, end 03:00
// Normal day: 00:00, 01:12, 02:24 -> 3 fires
// DST fall-back day: the 02:24 time is ambiguous (could be CEST or CET)
// GetUtcOffset prefers the MAX offset (daylight), so it picks 02:24 CEST (the first occurrence)
// Then the next fire would be 03:36... but endTimeOfDay is 03:00, so it should skip to next day

// Test 3: The original TestDayLightSaving test scenario
Console.WriteLine("\n--- Test 3: Original TestDayLightSaving scenario ---");
var tzUk = TimeZoneUtil.FindTimeZoneById("GMT Standard Time");
var trigger3 = DailyTimeIntervalScheduleBuilder.Create()
    .StartingDailyAt(TimeOfDay.HourAndMinuteOfDay(22, 15))
    .OnEveryDay()
    .WithIntervalInHours(24)
    .WithRepeatCount(9999)
    .InTimeZone(tzUk)
    .Build();

var first = trigger3.GetFireTimeAfter(new DateTimeOffset(2014, 10, 25, 0, 0, 0, TimeSpan.Zero));
Console.WriteLine($"First: {first} (expected: 2014-10-25 22:15:00 +01:00)");
var second = trigger3.GetFireTimeAfter(first);
Console.WriteLine($"Second: {second} (expected: 2014-10-26 22:15:00 +00:00)");
var third = trigger3.GetFireTimeAfter(second);
Console.WriteLine($"Third: {third} (expected: 2014-10-27 22:15:00 +00:00)");

// Test 4: TestFollowsTimeZone1 (spring forward for Eastern)
Console.WriteLine("\n--- Test 4: TestFollowsTimeZone1 (Eastern, spring forward) ---");
var tzEst = TimeZoneUtil.FindTimeZoneById("Eastern Standard Time");
var trigger4 = new DailyTimeIntervalTriggerImpl
{
    StartTimeUtc = new DateTimeOffset(2012, 3, 9, 23, 0, 0, TimeSpan.FromHours(-5)),
    StartTimeOfDay = new TimeOfDay(8, 0, 0),
    EndTimeOfDay = new TimeOfDay(11, 0, 0),
    RepeatIntervalUnit = IntervalUnit.Hour,
    RepeatInterval = 1,
    TimeZone = tzEst
};

var fireTimes4 = TriggerUtils.ComputeFireTimes(trigger4, null, 8);
Console.WriteLine($"Got {fireTimes4.Count} fire times:");
DateTimeOffset[] expected4 = {
    new DateTimeOffset(2012, 3, 10, 8, 0, 0, 0, TimeSpan.FromHours(-5)),
    new DateTimeOffset(2012, 3, 10, 9, 0, 0, 0, TimeSpan.FromHours(-5)),
    new DateTimeOffset(2012, 3, 10, 10, 0, 0, 0, TimeSpan.FromHours(-5)),
    new DateTimeOffset(2012, 3, 10, 11, 0, 0, 0, TimeSpan.FromHours(-5)),
    new DateTimeOffset(2012, 3, 11, 8, 0, 0, 0, TimeSpan.FromHours(-4)),
    new DateTimeOffset(2012, 3, 11, 9, 0, 0, 0, TimeSpan.FromHours(-4)),
    new DateTimeOffset(2012, 3, 11, 10, 0, 0, 0, TimeSpan.FromHours(-4)),
    new DateTimeOffset(2012, 3, 11, 11, 0, 0, 0, TimeSpan.FromHours(-4)),
};
bool allMatch = true;
for (int i = 0; i < expected4.Length; i++)
{
    bool match = fireTimes4[i] == expected4[i];
    Console.WriteLine($"  [{i}]: {fireTimes4[i]} {(match ? "OK" : $"FAIL (expected {expected4[i]})")}");
    if (!match) allMatch = false;
}
Console.WriteLine($"All match: {allMatch}");

// Test 5: TestFollowsTimeZone2 (fall back for Eastern)
Console.WriteLine("\n--- Test 5: TestFollowsTimeZone2 (Eastern, fall back) ---");
var trigger5 = new DailyTimeIntervalTriggerImpl
{
    StartTimeUtc = new DateTimeOffset(2012, 11, 2, 12, 0, 0, TimeSpan.FromHours(-4)),
    StartTimeOfDay = new TimeOfDay(8, 0, 0),
    EndTimeOfDay = new TimeOfDay(11, 0, 0),
    RepeatIntervalUnit = IntervalUnit.Hour,
    RepeatInterval = 1,
    TimeZone = tzEst
};

var fireTimes5 = TriggerUtils.ComputeFireTimes(trigger5, null, 8);
Console.WriteLine($"Got {fireTimes5.Count} fire times:");
DateTimeOffset[] expected5 = {
    new DateTimeOffset(2012, 11, 3, 8, 0, 0, 0, TimeSpan.FromHours(-4)),
    new DateTimeOffset(2012, 11, 3, 9, 0, 0, 0, TimeSpan.FromHours(-4)),
    new DateTimeOffset(2012, 11, 3, 10, 0, 0, 0, TimeSpan.FromHours(-4)),
    new DateTimeOffset(2012, 11, 3, 11, 0, 0, 0, TimeSpan.FromHours(-4)),
    new DateTimeOffset(2012, 11, 4, 8, 0, 0, 0, TimeSpan.FromHours(-5)),
    new DateTimeOffset(2012, 11, 4, 9, 0, 0, 0, TimeSpan.FromHours(-5)),
    new DateTimeOffset(2012, 11, 4, 10, 0, 0, 0, TimeSpan.FromHours(-5)),
    new DateTimeOffset(2012, 11, 4, 11, 0, 0, 0, TimeSpan.FromHours(-5)),
};
allMatch = true;
for (int i = 0; i < expected5.Length; i++)
{
    bool match = fireTimes5[i] == expected5[i];
    Console.WriteLine($"  [{i}]: {fireTimes5[i]} {(match ? "OK" : $"FAIL (expected {expected5[i]})")}");
    if (!match) allMatch = false;
}
Console.WriteLine($"All match: {allMatch}");

    public override DateTimeOffset? GetFireTimeAfter(DateTimeOffset? afterTime)
    {
        // Check if trigger has completed or not.
        if (complete)
        {
            return null;
        }

        // a. Increment afterTime by a second, so that we are comparing against a time after it!
        if (afterTime is null)
        {
            afterTime = TimeProvider.GetUtcNow().AddSeconds(1);
        }
        else
        {
            afterTime = afterTime.Value.AddSeconds(1);
        }

        // make sure afterTime is at least startTime
        if (afterTime < startTimeUtc)
        {
            afterTime = startTimeUtc;
        }

        // now change to local time zone
        afterTime = TimeZoneUtil.ConvertTime(afterTime.Value, TimeZone);

        // b.Check to see if afterTime is after endTimeOfDay or not.
        // If yes, then we need to advance to next day as well.
        bool afterTimePastEndTimeOfDay = false;
        if (endTimeOfDay is not null)
        {
            afterTimePastEndTimeOfDay = afterTime.Value > endTimeOfDay.GetTimeOfDayForDate(afterTime.Value);
        }

        // c. now we need to move to the next valid day of week if either:
        // the given time is past the end time of day, or given time is not on a valid day of week
        DateTimeOffset? fireTime = AdvanceToNextDayOfWeekIfNecessary(afterTime.Value, afterTimePastEndTimeOfDay);

        if (fireTime is null)
        {
            return null;
        }

        // d. Calculate and save fireTimeEndDate variable for later use
        DateTimeOffset fireTimeEndDate;
        if (endTimeOfDay is null)
        {
            fireTimeEndDate = new TimeOfDay(23, 59, 59).GetTimeOfDayForDate(fireTime.Value);
        }
        else
        {
            fireTimeEndDate = endTimeOfDay.GetTimeOfDayForDate(fireTime.Value);
        }

        // apply the proper offset for the end date
        fireTimeEndDate = new DateTimeOffset(fireTimeEndDate.DateTime, TimeZoneUtil.GetUtcOffset(fireTimeEndDate.DateTime, TimeZone));

        // e. Check fireTime against startTime or startTimeOfDay to see which go first.
        DateTimeOffset fireTimeStartDate = startTimeOfDay.GetTimeOfDayForDate(fireTime.Value);

        // apply the proper offset for the start date
        fireTimeStartDate = new DateTimeOffset(fireTimeStartDate.DateTime, TimeZoneUtil.GetUtcOffset(fireTimeStartDate.DateTime, TimeZone));

        if (fireTime < fireTimeStartDate)
        {
            return fireTimeStartDate.ToUniversalTime();
        }

        // f. Continue to calculate the fireTime by incremental unit of intervals.
        // recall that if fireTime was less that fireTimeStartDate, we didn't get this far
        // Use local time difference (wall clock) to correctly handle DST transitions
        long secondsAfterStart = (long) (fireTime.Value.DateTime - fireTimeStartDate.DateTime).TotalSeconds;
        long repeatLong = RepeatInterval;

        DateTime localFireTime = fireTimeStartDate.DateTime;
        IntervalUnit repeatUnit = RepeatIntervalUnit;
        long jumpCount = 0;
        if (repeatUnit == IntervalUnit.Second)
        {
            jumpCount = secondsAfterStart / repeatLong;
            if (secondsAfterStart % repeatLong != 0)
            {
                jumpCount++;
            }

            localFireTime = localFireTime.AddSeconds(RepeatInterval * (int) jumpCount);
        }
        else if (repeatUnit == IntervalUnit.Minute)
        {
            jumpCount = secondsAfterStart / (repeatLong * 60L);
            if (secondsAfterStart % (repeatLong * 60L) != 0)
            {
                jumpCount++;
            }
            localFireTime = localFireTime.AddMinutes(RepeatInterval * (int) jumpCount);
        }
        else if (repeatUnit == IntervalUnit.Hour)
        {
            jumpCount = secondsAfterStart / (repeatLong * 60L * 60L);
            if (secondsAfterStart % (repeatLong * 60L * 60L) != 0)
            {
                jumpCount++;
            }
            localFireTime = localFireTime.AddHours(RepeatInterval * (int) jumpCount);
        }

        // apply the proper offset for the new local fire time, handling DST transitions
        fireTime = new DateTimeOffset(localFireTime, TimeZoneUtil.GetUtcOffset(localFireTime, TimeZone));

        // g. Check if we've exceeded the per-day repeat count.
        if (repeatCount != RepeatIndefinitely && jumpCount > repeatCount)
        {
            fireTime = AdvanceToNextDayOfWeekIfNecessary(fireTime.Value, true);
            if (fireTime is null)
            {
                return null;
            }
            fireTime = startTimeOfDay.GetTimeOfDayForDate(fireTime);
            return fireTime?.ToUniversalTime();
        }

        // h. Ensure this new fireTime is within the day, or else we need to advance to next day.
        if (fireTime > fireTimeEndDate)
        {
            fireTime = AdvanceToNextDayOfWeekIfNecessary(fireTime.Value, IsSameDay(fireTime.Value, fireTimeEndDate));
            // make sure we hit the startTimeOfDay on the new day
            fireTime = startTimeOfDay.GetTimeOfDayForDate(fireTime);
        }

        // i. Return calculated fireTime.
        return fireTime?.ToUniversalTime();
    }

    private bool IsSameDay(DateTimeOffset d1, DateTimeOffset d2)

Let me now think if there are any other edge cases I might have missed:

1. **The `AdvanceToNextDayOfWeekIfNecessary` method**: This is called before the interval calculation and also when repeat count is exceeded or fireTime exceeds endTimeOfDay. When advancing to the next day, `startTimeOfDay.GetTimeOfDayForDate(fireTime)` is called. This uses the offset from `fireTime`, which should now be correct since `fireTime` has the correct offset from our fix.

2. **The `fireTimeEndDate` calculation**: This uses `endTimeOfDay.GetTimeOfDayForDate(fireTime.Value)` which uses `fireTime`'s offset, then applies the proper offset via `GetUtcOffset`. This should be fine.

3. **The comparison `if (fireTime > fireTimeEndDate)`**: Both have correct offsets now, so the comparison is correct.

4. **What about when `fireTime` falls exactly on an ambiguous time?** `GetUtcOffset` returns the MAX offset (daylight time) for ambiguous times. This means it picks the first occurrence of the ambiguous time. For `localFireTime.AddHours(...)`, if the result falls in the ambiguous period (e.g., 02:30 during fall-back), `GetUtcOffset` will return the daylight offset (e.g., +02:00 for CEST). This is consistent with the existing behavior of `GetUtcOffset`.

5. **What about when `fireTime` falls on an invalid time (spring forward)?** `DateTime.AddHours` could produce a DateTime that doesn't exist (e.g., 02:30 during spring forward when clocks jump from 02:00 to 03:00). `GetUtcOffset` would throw an exception for invalid times. However, this is an edge case that was already present in the original code (if the UTC-based addition coincidentally landed on an invalid local time, the same exception would occur). My fix doesn't make this worse.

Let me verify the spring-forward edge case more carefully. In Test 1 above, we start from 00:01:05 and add 24 hours. That gives 00:01:05 next day, which is always valid. But what about intervals that don't divide evenly into 24 hours?

- Fire times: 01:30, 02:30, 03:30, 04:30...
- But 02:30 doesn't exist (it's skipped).

- `secondsAfterStart = (01:30 - 01:30) = 0`

- `afterTime` = 2020-03-29 00:30:00 UTC + 1s = 2020-03-29 00:30:01 UTC
- `ConvertTime` to CET = 2020-03-29 01:30:01 CET (+01:00)
- `fireTimeStartDate` = 2020-03-29 01:30:00 +01:00
- `fireTime` (01:30:01) > `fireTimeStartDate` (01:30:00)
- `secondsAfterStart = 01:30:01 - 01:30:00 = 1 second`
- `jumpCount = 1 / 3600 = 0`, remainder != 0, so jumpCount = 1
- `localFireTime = 01:30:00.AddHours(1)` = 02:30:00
- `GetUtcOffset(2020-03-29 02:30:00, CET)` → this is an invalid time!

using System;

var tz = TimeZoneInfo.FindSystemTimeZoneById("Central European Standard Time");

// March 29, 2020 02:30:00 is invalid (DST spring forward, clocks go from 02:00 to 03:00)
var invalidTime = new DateTime(2020, 3, 29, 2, 30, 0);

Console.WriteLine($"IsAmbiguousTime: {tz.IsAmbiguousTime(invalidTime)}");

try {
    var offset = tz.GetUtcOffset(invalidTime);
    Console.WriteLine($"Offset for invalid time: {offset}");
} catch (Exception ex) {
    Console.WriteLine($"Exception: {ex.GetType().Name}: {ex.Message}");

// The offset for 03:30 should be +02:00

Console.WriteLine($"IsInvalidTime(03:30): {tz.IsInvalidTime(validTime)}");

2026-05-29 09:51:15,994 - INFO - swea-agent - 💭 THOUGHT
So .NET's `TimeZoneInfo.GetUtcOffset` returns the standard time offset (+01:00) for invalid times instead of throwing. This means our code produces 02:30 CET (+01:00) = 01:30 UTC, which when displayed in local timezone is 03:30 CEST (since 02:30 CET would be 03:30 in CEST... no, that's not right).

Wait, the output says:
```
03/29/2020 01:30:00 +00:00 -> UTC=03/29/2020 01:30:00, TZ local=03/29/2020 03:30:00 +02:00
```

So the fire time is 01:30 UTC, which when converted to the target timezone gives 03:30 CEST. This is actually the correct behavior! After 01:30 CET, the next logical fire time at 02:30 doesn't exist, so the next valid time would be 03:30 CEST. The code produces this by a "quirk" of .NET's `GetUtcOffset` returning +01:00 for the invalid 02:30, which makes the DateTimeOffset 02:30 +01:00 = 01:30 UTC. Then when converted back to CET, 01:30 UTC on March 29 is 03:30 CEST (since DST has started, offset is +02:00).

Actually, this is the same behavior as the old code would have produced! The old code would have done:
- `sTime = fireTimeStartDate.ToUniversalTime()` = 2020-03-29 00:30:00 UTC
- `sTime.AddHours(1)` = 2020-03-29 01:30:00 UTC
- `ConvertTime(01:30 UTC, CET)` = 2020-03-29 03:30:00 CEST (+02:00)

So the result is the same. Good.

Now I'm confident the fix is correct and handles edge cases properly.

Let me also check if the `GetUtcOffset` behavior for ambiguous times (fall-back) is consistent with what we want. During fall-back, when clocks go from 2:00 AM back to 1:00 AM (or 3:00 AM back to 2:00 AM depending on timezone), times between 2:00-3:00 occur twice. `GetUtcOffset` returns the MAX offset (daylight/summer time), which is the FIRST occurrence. This is documented in the code comment:

```csharp
// Unlike the default behavior of TimeZoneInfo.GetUtcOffset, it is prefered to choose
// the DAYLIGHT time when the input is ambiguous, because the daylight instance is the
// FIRST instance, and time moves in a forward direction.
```

This is correct because when scheduling, you want the first occurrence of an ambiguous time, not the second.
